Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
Praying with an Impure Garment: The Lesser of Two Evils
Resolving the ikhtilaf on praying in a najis garment vs. naked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-school position on praying with an impure garment and apply the principle of choosing the lesser evil.

Core Idea
When forced between two harms, choose the one with a substitute or fewer abandoned obligations.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary from Fath al-Qadir presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about a person who has only an impure garment. Should he pray in it despite the impurity, or pray naked with gestures? The answer involves the principle of 'ahwan al-baliyatayn' (the lesser of two evils) and the concept of badal (substitute).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The case is a person who has only a garment that is impure (over a quarter). He cannot clean or replace it. What are his options?
The text distinguishes between impurity less than a quarter (valid) and more than a quarter (problematic).
2
State the position of Zufar and Muhammad
Zufar and Muhammad (within the Hanafi school) oblige praying in the impure garment with full movements, because the command to cover remains while purification is excused.
They argue that praying in the garment abandons only one obligation (purity), while naked prayer abandons multiple.
3
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and relied upon)
Abu Hanifa gives a choice between praying in the impure garment (standing with bowing/prostration) or praying naked with gestures, but prefers the former.
The mufta bihi is this position of choice, with the garment option being better.
4
Analyze the evidence
The Hanafi evidence includes: (1) the command to cover with a pure garment falls when unable, (2) the principle of choosing the lesser evil, (3) the hadith of the Companions on the ship who prayed naked with gestures.
The hadith is considered near-consensus (ijma' suknuti).
5
Understand the response to the objection
The response is that gestures (iima') serve as a badal for standing, bowing, and prostration, so no obligations are truly abandoned. The substitute stands in place of the original.
This is similar to the rider in supererogatory prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وجد ثوباً إلخ أي فإن كان الأكثر من الربع طاهراً أولى أن لا تجوز صلاته؛ لأن الربع يحكي حكاية الكل، وهذا إذا لم يجد ما يزيل به النجاسة ولا ما يقللها صلى معها و لم يعد ، ولا يجوز صلاته عرياناً. (فتح) لم تجز: صلاته لأن للربع حكم الكل كما في الإحرام. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٠/١] وخير بين أن يصلي عريانا قاعدا بإيماء وبين أن يصلي قائما بركوع وسجود وهو أفضل، وكذا إذا كان كله متنجساً؛ لأن النظر إليهما بسبب للفتنه. (ع)] وقال زفر ومحمد: لزمه أن يصلي فيه بركوع وسجود، ولا يجوز له أن يصلي عرياناً؛ لأن خطاب التطهير سقط عنه لعجزه و لم يسقط عنه خطاب الستر لقدرته عليه، فصار بمنزلة الطاهر في حقه؛ ولأن في الصلاة فيه ترك فرض واحد، وهو طهارة الثوب النجس، وفي الصلاة عرياناً ترك فروض من ستر العورة والقيام والركوع والسجود ، ولنا أن المأمور به الستر بالطاهر، فإذا لم يقدر عليه سقط، فيميل إلى أيها شاء، والجواب عن ترك الفروض أنه وإن صلى قاعداً قد أتى ببدلها، وهو الإيماء، فلا يكون تاركاً لها لقيام البدل مقام الأصل، والأصل في جنس هذه المسألة أن من ابتلي ببليتين يختار أهونهما؛ لأن مباشرة الحرام لا تجوز إلا لضرورة، مثاله: رجل لو قام وركع وسجد ينفلت ريحه، وإن جلس ويؤمئ لا ينفلت فيصلى قاعداً بإيماء؛ لأن ترك القيام والركوع والسجود أهون؛ لأن له عوضاً، وقيد تقيد تركه في بعض الصور كالتطوع على الدابة. (فتح) ولو عدم ثوبا إلخ أراد بالثوب ما يستر عورته، وبالعدم عدم القدرة حتى لو أبيح له ثوب ثبتت القدرة على الأصح، وإذا وعد به ينتظر ، ولو قدر عليه بالشراء بثمن المثل وله ثمنه يلزمه الشراء، وإلا صلى قاعداً مؤمياً؛ لما روى أنس بن مالك أن أصحاب رسول الله الله ركبوا في السفينة فانكسرت بهم السفينة، فخرجوا من البحر عرياناً فصلوا قعوداً بالإيماء، وهذا قول روي عنهم، و لم يرو عن أقرانهم خلاف ذلك، فجعل محل الإجماع. (فتح، مستخلص) ثوباً : أي ساتراً ولو حريراً أو نباتاً أو طيناً يلطخها به. (ط) قاعدا نهارا أو ليلا في بيت أو صحراء. (فتح)
And if he finds a garment, etc. – i.e., if the majority of the quarter is pure, then it is more appropriate that his prayer is not valid, because the quarter represents the whole. This is when he does not find anything to remove the impurity nor anything to reduce it; he prays in it and does not repeat, and his prayer is not valid while naked. (Fath) It is not valid: his prayer because the quarter has the ruling of the whole, as in ihram. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/50] And he is given a choice between praying naked sitting with gestures and praying standing with bowing and prostration, and the latter is better. Likewise if the entire garment is impure, because looking at them is a cause of fitnah. (A) Zufar and Muhammad said: He must pray in it with bowing and prostration, and it is not permissible for him to pray naked, because the command of purification falls from him due to his inability, but the command of covering does not fall from him because he is able to do it. So he becomes like the pure with respect to it. And because in praying in it there is abandoning one obligation, which is the purity of the impure garment, whereas in praying naked there is abandoning obligations: covering the private parts, standing, bowing, and prostration. But our [Hanafi] evidence is that what is commanded is covering with a pure [garment]. If he is unable to do so, then it falls [from him], and he inclines to whichever he wishes. The answer concerning the abandoning of obligations is that even if he prays sitting, he is performing a substitute (badal) for them, which is gestures (iima'), so he is not abandoning them, because the substitute stands in the place of the original. The general principle in this class of issue is that one who is faced with two afflictions chooses the lesser of them, because directly committing the forbidden is not permissible except due to necessity. Example: A man who, if he stands, bows, and prostrates, breaks wind, but if he sits and gestures, he does not break wind, so he prays sitting with gestures, because abandoning standing, bowing, and prostration is lighter because they have a substitute, and the restriction of their omission is in some cases like supererogatory prayer on a mount. (Fath) And if he does not have a garment, etc. – by 'garment' he means something that covers his private parts, and by 'lack' is lack of ability, such that even if he is allowed a garment, his ability is established according to the most correct view. And if it is promised, he waits. And if he is able [to get it] by purchasing it for the equivalent price and he has its price, he is obliged to purchase. Otherwise, he prays sitting with gestures, as narrated by Anas ibn Malik that the Companions of the Messenger of Allah (may peace be upon him) rode on a ship, and the ship broke, so they came out of the sea naked and prayed sitting with gestures. This is a statement narrated from them, and no contrary has been narrated from their peers, so it is considered a place of consensus. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'A garment': i.e., a cover, even if it is silk, or plants, or mud that he smears himself with. (T) 'Sitting': by day or night, in a house or desert. (Fath)
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who has only an impure garment (najis) to wear during prayer. The text first clarifies that if the garment has impurity on less than a quarter of its area, the prayer is valid. But if a quarter or more is impure, the ruling becomes problematic. The main dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa (with his two disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Zufar and Muhammad (in one narration). Zufar and Muhammad argue that the person must pray in the impure garment with standing, bowing, and prostration, and cannot pray naked, because the obligation of purification (taharah) from impurity falls due to inability, but the obligation of covering the 'awrah does not fall since he can cover it with the garment. They claim that praying in the najis garment abandons only one obligation (purity of garment), while praying naked abandons multiple obligations (covering, standing, etc.). The Hanafi position (attributed to Abu Hanifa and relied upon) is that the person has a choice between praying naked with gestures (iima') or praying in the impure garment with full movements. However, the preferred option is to pray in the impure garment standing with bowing and prostration, because it is closer to the normal form of prayer. Yet Abu Hanifa's reasoning is different: the command is to cover with a pure garment; if unable, the command falls. The person then chooses the lesser evil. The response to Zufar/Muhammad is that if a person prays sitting with gestures, he is not truly abandoning the obligations; he is performing them through substitutes (gestures represent standing, bowing, etc.), as a rider in voluntary prayer. The principle is choosing the lighter of two afflictions. The text further explains that if a person lacks any garment, he must pray sitting with gestures, citing the hadith of the Companions on the ship as evidence, which is considered near-consensus. The definition of 'garment' includes any cover, even silk, plants, or mud. The prayer is performed sitting whether by day or night.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmā’): Gestural movements (bowing and prostration indicated by head movements) performed while sitting, used when unable to perform full physical movements.
بدل (badal): Substitute or replacement for an obligatory action when the original is impossible, such as iima' for standing and bowing.
أهون البليتين (ahwan al-baliyatayn): The lesser of two evils; a principle applied when forced to choose between two prohibited or harmful actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, which of the following is true for someone who only has a najis garment?
A) He must pray in it.
B) He must pray naked.
C) He may choose, but praying in it is better.
D) He should wait until he finds a pure garment.

Key Takeaway
When forced between praying in an impure garment or praying naked, the Hanafi school permits choosing the lesser evil, and substitutes (badal) preserve the obligations.

Facing the Qibla: General Rule and Exception for the Frightened
Sets general qibla rule and exception for the frightened.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general obligation for facing the qibla and identify the exception for the frightened person (al-kha'if) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
For non-Makkans, facing the direction of the Kaaba suffices; the frightened pray to any direction due to valid excuse.

Facing the qibla is a fundamental condition for prayer. But what if one cannot determine the direction or is genuinely unable to face it? In this lesson, we learn the general rule for non-Makkans and the specific exception for the frightened person (al-kha'if), along with the underlying rationale from the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage distinguishes between the Meccan, who must face the Kaaba building itself, and the non-Meccan, who only needs to face its direction. Understand this distinction and which applies to you.
The text states: 'for other than him (the Meccan), it is facing its direction'.
2
Define al-kha'if (the frightened)
Al-kha'if is defined as anyone with a valid excuse preventing him from facing the qibla, including fear of an enemy, thief, or wild animal, or inability due to illness or lack of assistance.
The commentary expands this to include the sick and those on a plank in the sea.
3
Understand the ruling for al-kha'if
The frightened person prays to any direction he is able. The prayer is valid even if he does not face the qibla at all, because the Kaaba is not worshipped for its own sake, but as a test. When genuine incapacity exists, the test is fulfilled by the effort.
The text says: 'wa al-kha'ifu yusalli ila ayyi jihatin qadara'.
4
Note the extensions and rationale
The same ruling applies to the sick who cannot be turned towards the qibla and to one on a plank in the sea. The rationale is that the Kaaba is a means, not an end; the ultimate purpose is devotion, which is achieved despite the inability.
The commentary from Fath al-Qadir explicitly extends the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولغيره إصابة جهتها، والخائف يصلّى إلى أي جهة قدر. إصابة جهتها: أي التوجه إلى جهة الكعبة في الصحيح (ع) وعن المكي: طف الكعبة. والخائف: أي من له عذر يمنع من التوجه إليها، سواء كان خوفا من عدو أو لص أو سبع، إن صلى إلى جهة الكعبة أو لا كعدم الاستطاعة على التوجه إليها لضعف مرض أو من غيره، ولا يجد من يوجهه إليها. والفقه فيه أن المصلي في خدمة الله تعالى فلابد من الإقبال عليه، وهو منزه عن الجهة، فابتلاه بالتوجه إلى الكعبة، فلما اعتراه الخوف تحقق العذر، فأشبه حالة الاشتباه في تحقق العذر، فيتوجه إلى غير أي جهة قدر؛ لأن الكعبة لم تعبد لعينها حتى لو سجد لها كفي بل للابتلاء وهو حاصل بذلك. (فتح) أي جهة قدر : لتحقق العجز، وكذا المريض إذا لم يجد من يحوله إليها ومن كان على خشبة في البحر. (ع)
And for other than him (the Meccan), it is facing its direction; and the frightened one prays to any direction he is able. 'Facing its direction' means turning towards the direction of the Kaaba according to the sound view, and concerning the Meccan: (one must face) the building of the Kaaba. And 'the frightened one' is one who has an excuse preventing him from turning towards it, whether it be fear from an enemy, a thief, or a wild beast, whether he prays towards the direction of the Kaaba or not, such as inability to face it due to weakness from illness or other, and he finds no one to direct him towards it. The legal reasoning is that the prayer is in the service of Allah, so he must face Him, and He is free from direction, so He tested him by facing the Kaaba. When fear overcomes him, the excuse is realized, so it resembles the case of ambiguity in realizing the excuse. So he turns towards any direction he is able, because the Kaaba is not worshipped for itself such that if he prostrated to it it would suffice; rather it is for the test, and that is achieved by doing so. (Fath) 'Any direction he is able' due to the realization of incapability, and similarly the sick person if he does not find someone to turn him towards it, and the one on a plank in the sea.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, with commentary from the sharh. It first establishes the general obligation for non-Makkans: they must face the direction of the Kaaba. For the Meccan, the obligation is more specific: he must face the Kaaba building itself. Then it introduces the exception for the frightened person (al-kha'if), defined as one with a valid excuse such as fear of an enemy, thief, or wild animal, or inability due to illness or lack of guidance. Such a person is permitted to pray in any direction he is able. The reasoning (fiqh) is that since Allah is beyond direction, the purpose of facing the Kaaba is a test of devotion. When one is unable to determine or face the exact direction due to fear or incapacity, the test is fulfilled by making an effort, and the prayer is valid. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir extends this to the sick person who cannot be turned and the one on a plank in the sea.

Key Terms
الخائف (al-kha'if): One who has a valid excuse preventing him from facing the qibla, such as fear of an enemy, thief, or wild animal, or inability due to illness or lack of assistance.
إصابة جهتها (isabat jihataha): Facing the direction of the Kaaba, not the Kaaba itself, for those outside Makka.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is included in the definition of al-kha'if?
A) Only someone fleeing from an enemy
B) Someone unable to face the qibla due to illness or lack of guidance
C) Anyone who is in doubt about the qibla direction
D) Only someone in battle

Key Takeaway
The obligation to face the qibla is relaxed for those with a valid excuse, following the principle that Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.

Realizing Qibla Error During Prayer: Turning in Place
Presents the ruling on correcting qibla direction during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on realizing qibla error during prayer and identify the conditions under which one must turn and continue without restarting.

Core Idea
Realizing qibla error during prayer requires immediate turning, not restarting.

Imagine you are in the middle of prayer and suddenly realize you are facing the wrong direction. What should you do? The Hanafi ruling is clear: you must turn immediately to the correct qibla and continue your prayer from where you left off. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its basis in the incident of Masjid Quba, and the conditions that trigger this obligation. The goal is to equip you with the precise legal framework so you can apply it confidently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Recognize that the ruling concerns a person who becomes aware of the correct qibla while already engaged in prayer. The required action is immediate turning (istidarah) and continuation of the prayer.
The prayer is not invalidated; it continues.
2
Establish the Trigger Condition
Determine the condition that obligates turning: the prayer must still be ongoing, and the person must have reliable knowledge (e.g., from a trustworthy person or clear signs) of the correct direction.
Knowledge after the prayer ends does not apply.
3
Understand the Basis (Dalil)
Recall the historical incident of the companions at Masjid Quba. When they learned of the qibla change from Jerusalem to the Kaaba, they turned in their prayer without restarting, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) approved.
This serves as the foundational proof (dalil) for the ruling.
4
Apply the Ruling to All Stages of Prayer
Note that the ruling applies regardless of when knowledge occurs during the prayer—even after sitting for the tashahhud or during sajdat al-sahw. The commentary (Fath al-Qadir) emphasizes this universality.
No special exceptions for late realization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن علم به في صلاته استدار. فإن علم به بأن أخبره من هو عالم بحالها أو بعلامات أخر، وهو في الصلاة يجب عليه أن يتحول من ساعته في الصلاة وليس عليه أن يستأنف، والأصل في هذه المسألة قصة الأنصار بمسجد قباء وتحولهم في الصلاة إلى القبلة، واستحسان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فعلهم. وفي إطلاق كلام المصنف إشارة إلى أنه لو علم بالخطأ استدار، وإن كان بعد ما قعد قدر التشهد أو في سجود السهو. (فتح) استدار: أي إلى القبلة وأتم؛ لأن أهل قباء لما بلغهم نسخ القبلة استداروا في الصلاة كهيئتهم. (ع)
And if he becomes aware of it during his prayer, he turns. If he becomes aware, by being informed by someone knowledgeable about it, or by other signs, and he is in the prayer, he must turn immediately during the prayer and does not have to restart. The basis of this issue is the story of the Ansar in Masjid Quba, and they turned during the prayer towards the qibla, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) approved of their action. And from the absolute wording of the author there is an indication that if he knows of the error, he turns, even if it was after he sat for the amount of the tashahhud or during the prostration of forgetfulness. (Fath) 'He turns' means towards the qibla and completes, because when the people of Quba received the abrogation of the qibla, they turned in the prayer as they were.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This ruling statement addresses the scenario where a person realizes the correct qibla direction while he is already in prayer. The text rules that he must turn immediately towards the qibla and continue his prayer; he does not need to restart. The basis is the well-known incident of the companions at Masjid Quba: when they were informed that the qibla had been changed from Jerusalem to the Kaaba, they turned in their prayer immediately, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) approved. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir emphasizes that turning is required even if the realization occurs after sitting for the tashahhud or during sajdat al-sahw. The ruling applies regardless of when the knowledge comes, as long as he is still in the prayer.

Key Terms
استدار (istadāra): To turn in place towards the correct qibla during prayer without breaking it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what should a person do if he realizes the correct qibla during his prayer?
A) Break the prayer and restart from the beginning
B) Turn towards the qibla and continue, no restart needed
C) Complete the prayer in the original direction and repeat later
D) Make a separate prostration of forgetfulness

Key Takeaway
Upon realizing qibla error during prayer, turn immediately and continue; do not restart.

Congregational Prayer with Different Qibla Directions Without Knowing Imam's Direction
Ruling on validity of congregational prayer with different qibla directions due to ijtihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the validity of congregational prayer when followers face different qibla directions due to ijtihad and do not know the imam's direction, and identify the two exceptions that invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
When followers ijtihad for qibla and the imam's direction is unknown, their prayer is valid unless the follower is certain the imam is wrong or ahead.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a practical scenario when the qibla is ambiguous and followers have different opinions. The ruling establishes that congregational prayer remains valid despite differing directions, as long as the follower does not hold a belief that the imam is mistaken or out of position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario: a group of followers perform ijtihad, face different directions, and are ignorant of the imam's direction.
Ignorance here means they do not know which direction the imam chose.
2
State the general ruling
The matn says 'yujzihim' – the prayer suffices, i.e., it is valid.
This is the default ruling.
3
Identify the first exception
If a follower is certain that the imam is facing a different direction, his prayer becomes invalid because he believes the imam to be in error.
Certainty, not mere doubt, triggers invalidity.
4
Identify the second exception
If a follower is certain that the imam has preceded him in performance (e.g., the imam is not in front), the prayer is invalid because he abandoned the condition of standing (following behind).
This refers to the imam being out of position relative to the follower.
5
Explain the rationale
The underlying principle: the follower's belief about the imam's correctness is crucial. As long as the follower assumes the imam is correct (by being ignorant of any error), the connection (iqtida) is sound.
Certainty of error breaks the necessary trust in the imam's leadership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تحرى قوم جهات، وجهلوا حال إمامهم يجزيهم. قال في الفتح: قوم أي جماعة مع الإمام عند اشتباه القبلة. (ع) يجزيهم تلك الصلاة إذا كانوا خلف الإمام؛ لأن القبلة في حقهم جهة التحري، ومن تيقن منهم مخالفة إمامه في الجهة أو تقدمه عليه حالة الأداء لم تجز صلاته؛ لأنه اعتقد إمامه على الخطأ في الأولى وترك فرض المقام في الثانية. (ع)
And if a group of people make ijtihad (towards different) directions, and they are ignorant of the state (direction) of their imam, it suffices them. (Fath) 'Qawm' means a congregation with an imam when the qibla is ambiguous. (Ayn) That prayer suffices them if they are behind the imam, because the qibla for them is the direction of ijtihad. And whoever is certain that his imam is opposite in direction, or that the imam preceded him in performance, his prayer is not valid, because he believed his imam to be in error in the first case and abandoned the condition of standing in the second.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This ruling addresses a specific scenario in congregational prayer when the qibla is ambiguous. The matn states that if each follower performs ijtihad and faces a different direction, and they are unaware of the imam's direction, the prayer is valid. The commentary clarifies that the qibla for them is the direction of their ijtihad. However, if any follower is certain that the imam is facing a different direction (and thus believes the imam is incorrect), his prayer is invalid because he holds a belief that the imam is in error. Similarly, if he believes the imam has moved ahead of him in the prayer (e.g., leading from behind), his prayer is invalid. The key point is that validity depends on the follower's belief regarding the imam's correctness.

Key Terms
جهات (jihāt): Different directions; each follower faces the result of his own ijtihad.
تحرى (taḥarrā): To make ijtihad, to exert effort to determine the qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a follower's prayer in this situation considered invalid according to the passage?
A) If he faces a different direction from other followers
B) If he is certain that the imam is facing a different direction
C) If he does not know the imam's direction
D) If he performs ijtihad without asking the imam

Key Takeaway
The validity of congregational prayer when qibla is ambiguous depends on the follower's knowledge and belief regarding the imam's direction; ignorance preserves validity, while certainty of error or of improper position invalidates.

When Ijtihad Yields No Qibla Direction
Ruling for one whose ijtihad does not indicate any direction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for qibla ijtihad when no direction is preferred and explain the legal logic behind praying to all four directions.

Core Idea
When ijtihad yields no qibla direction, pray to each of the four directions once.

This lesson covers a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the qibla. When a person attempts to determine the direction of prayer through ijtihad but cannot reach any conclusion, the school provides a clear solution: pray one complete prayer to each cardinal direction. This ensures that one of the prayers is correct. The ruling reflects the school's practical approach to extreme uncertainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
Recognize that this ruling applies only when a person performs ijtihad for qibla but cannot form any preference (tahayyur).
Ijtihad involves using available signs (sun, stars, landmarks) to determine qibla.
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi ruling requires the person to pray one complete salat to each of the four cardinal directions (north, south, east, west).
The text says 'prays to each direction once'.
3
Understand the legal logic
By praying to all directions, the person ensures that at least one prayer is offered in the correct qibla. This is a practical solution that respects the obligation of qibla without causing undue hardship.
This is an application of the principle of darurah (necessity) and ihtiyat (precaution).
4
Note practical implications
The person must perform four complete prayers, one in each direction. This may involve repeating the prayer if one direction is later confirmed correct.
Some later Hanafi scholars discuss repeating the prayers only if time allows, but the ruling is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لم يقع تحريه على شيء صلى لكل جهة مرة. (ع)
And one whose ijtihad does not fall upon anything (no clear direction) prays to each direction once.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This ruling covers the extreme case where a person attempts ijtihad for the qibla but cannot reach any conclusion or preference. In such a situation, the Hanafi ruling is that he must pray one complete prayer to each of the four cardinal directions. This ensures that one of the prayers will have been offered in the correct direction. The ruling appears as a marginal note (marked with 'ayn) in the text. It is a practical solution for when all signs fail.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Ijtihad or effort to determine the qibla direction using available signs.
جهة (jiha): Direction; here the four cardinal directions (north, south, east, west).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When ijtihad for qibla fails to yield any preference, one must pray to each of the four cardinal directions to ensure fulfillment of the obligation.

Sufficiency of al-Fatiha in Prayer
States the ruling on reciting al-Fatiha alone in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on reciting al-Fatiha in obligatory prayer and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Reciting al-Fatiha is sunnah in the Hanafi school; the alternate wajib view requires sajdah al-sahw.

This passage addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: is reciting al-Fatiha in obligatory prayer obligatory (wajib) or just a confirmed sunnah? The difference carries practical consequences, particularly whether leaving it requires sajdah al-sahw. Let's unpack the views and see which one is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the general Hanafi stance on reciting al-Fatiha in obligatory prayers as presented in the matn.
The matn says 'He sufficed with al-Fatiha,' implying it is sufficient and not compulsory.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi variant
Note that Imam Abu Hanifa has a different transmission making al-Fatiha wajib and requiring sajdah al-sahw for omission.
This is a riwayah from Abu Hanifa, not the majority view of his students.
3
Analyse the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold it is sunnah, so no sajdah is needed.
Their position aligns with the relied-upon view.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if one omits al-Fatiha, does he need to perform sajdah al-sahw? According to Abu Hanifa's view, yes; according to the mufta bihi, no.
Also, substituting tasbih or silence is permissible in the sunnah view.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text says 'as-sahih al-awwal' (the first is correct), meaning the sunnah position is relied upon.
Thus, the operative ruling is that reciting al-Fatiha is sunnah, not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اكتفى بالفاتحة: وإن شاء تركها، وعن أبي حنيفة أنها واجبة حتى يجب سجود السهو بتركها، والصحيح الأول حتى لو سبح ثلاثاً أو سكت قدرها جاز.] أي مع غنية له عن قراءتها، فإنها سنة على الظاهر، وهذا عندنا في الفرائض، أما في النوافل فضم السورة واجب كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى. (فتح)
He sufficed with al-Fatiha: And if he wishes he may leave it. And from Abu Hanifa that it is obligatory such that the prostration of forgetfulness becomes necessary by leaving it. And the correct is the first, such that even if he glorified three times or remained silent for its duration, it is permissible. That is, even if he is free from the need to recite it, for it is sunnah according to the apparent view. And this in our school in the obligatory prayers. As for supererogatory prayers, joining a surah is obligatory as will come, God willing. (Fath)
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of reciting al-Fatiha in prayer. The matn states that one may suffice with al-Fatiha, implying it is not obligatory. The commentary explains that according to Abu Hanifa, it is wajib (obligatory) such that leaving it necessitates sajdah al-sahw. However, the relied-upon position (sahih) is that it is not wajib; one may substitute it with tasbih or silence of equal duration. The commentary clarifies that this is the ruling for obligatory prayers (fara'id), while in nafl prayers, adding a surah is obligatory (wajib).

Key Terms
اكتفى بالفاتحة (iktafā bil-fātiḥah): He sufficed with al-Fatiha, meaning it is enough to recite only al-Fatiha without adding another surah.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness required when a wajib action is omitted or delayed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is wajib, leaving it requires sajdah al-sahw.
C) It is sunnah, leaving it is permissible without compensation.
D) It is makruh to recite it alone.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view is that reciting al-Fatiha is sunnah in obligatory prayers, so omitting it or substituting it with tasbih does not invalidate the prayer.

Definition of Imamate: Greater and Lesser
Defines the two types of imamate and their conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the greater and lesser imamate, state their conditions, and explain the obligation of appointing a caliph.

Core Idea
Imamate has two meanings: political leadership (caliphate) and leading prayer; each has distinct conditions.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq defines imamate in two senses: the greater imamate (imāmah kubrā), which is the general political leadership of the Muslim community, and the lesser imamate (imāmah ṣughrā), which is leading congregational prayer. The author lists conditions for each, emphasizing that appointing a caliph is a collective obligation, while the prayer imam must meet specific ritual qualifications. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion in legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of imamate
Locate the terms 'al-kubra' and 'al-sughra' in the passage. Note that the passage first lists conditions for the prayer imam, then defines the greater and lesser imamate.
The passage begins with general conditions for imamate in the context of prayer before distinguishing the two types.
2
Extract conditions for the greater imamate
Read the list of conditions for the caliph: freedom, Islam, masculinity, sanity, adulthood, capability. Also note the factors that cause removal (apostasy, insanity, captivity, etc.).
The greater imamate is a collective obligation (fard kifayah), as stated by the author.
3
Extract conditions for the lesser imamate
Identify the conditions for the prayer leader: puberty, Islam, sanity, masculinity, sufficient Quran memorization, and being healthy without excuse. These are listed at the beginning of the passage.
These conditions are specific to the act of leading prayer, not for political leadership.
4
Understand the wisdom behind the lesser imamate
The passage explains that the lesser imamate is prescribed to establish harmony and allow the ignorant to learn from the scholar. This wisdom justifies its recommendation.
This wisdom is unique to the prayer imamate and not applicable to the caliphate.
5
Compare the two types
The greater imamate is a political obligation with stricter removal conditions, while the lesser imamate is a ritual act with conditions focused on validity of prayer.
The conditions for removal from caliphate (e.g., blindness, illness) do not necessarily disqualify one from leading prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإمامة لها شروط، وهي البلوغ والإسلام والعقل والذكورة وحفظ من القرآن قدر ما يجزئ، وأن يكون الإمام صحيحاً لا عذر به (فتح)] وهي الصغرى والكبرى، فالكبرى استحقاق تصرف عام، ونصب الإمام من أهم الواجبات، فلهذا قدموه على دفن صاحب المعجزات ويشترط كونه حراً مسلماً ذكرًا عاقلاً بالغاً قادراً، ويكره تقليد الفاسق ويعزل به وينعزل بطريان ما يفوت المقصود من الردة والجنون المطبق وصيرورته أسيرا لا يرجى خلاصه، والعمى والخرس والصمم والمرض الذي ينسي العلوم وخلعه نفسه عن الإمامة لعجزه. والصغرى ربط صلاة المقتدي بصلاة الإمام، أو اتباع المصلي في جزء من صلاته، فالإمام هو المتبوع، والحكمة في ذلك قيام نظام الألفة بين المصلين، ولهذا شرعت في مساجد المحال؛ ليحصل التعاهد باللقاء في الأوقات، وليتعلم الجاهل من العالم الصلاة. (فتح)
The chapter of imamate has conditions: puberty, Islam, sanity, masculinity, memorization of the Qur'an to the extent that suffices, and that the imam be healthy without excuse (Fath). And it is the minor and major [imamate]. The major is the entitlement of general disposal, and appointing the imam is among the most important obligations; for this reason they gave it precedence over burying the master of miracles. And it is required that he be free, Muslim, male, sane, adult, capable. It is disliked to appoint the sinful, and he is removed, and he becomes removed by the occurrence of what frustrates the purpose: apostasy, continuous insanity, becoming a captive from whom release is not hoped, blindness, dumbness, deafness, illness that causes forgetfulness of knowledge, and his self-removal from imamate due to inability. And the minor [imamate] is the connection of the follower's prayer to the imam's prayer, or the following of the praying person in a part of his prayer. So the imam is the one followed, and the wisdom in that is the establishment of the system of harmony among the worshippers. For this reason it was prescribed in the mosques of the districts so that mutual engagement occurs through meeting at the times, and so that the ignorant learns prayer from the scholar. (Fath)
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage defines imamate in two senses: the greater imamate (imāmah kubrā), which is the general political leadership of the Muslim community, and the lesser imamate (imāmah ṣughrā), which is the act of leading congregational prayer. The author, al-Nasafi, begins by listing the conditions for a valid imam in the context of prayer: puberty, Islam, sanity, masculinity, and sufficient knowledge of Qur'an to complete the prayer. He then turns to the greater imamate, noting that appointing a caliph is a collective obligation (farḍ kifāyah) and was prioritized so highly that the Companions delayed the burial of the Prophet to appoint Abu Bakr. The conditions for the caliph are freedom, Islam, masculinity, sanity, adulthood, and capability. It is disliked to appoint a sinful person, and the imam is removed if he loses qualification through apostasy, insanity, captivity, etc. The lesser imamate is defined as the follower connecting his prayer to the imam's prayer, with the wisdom of fostering unity and teaching the ignorant. The commentary (Fath al-Qadir) elaborates on these points.

Key Terms
الإمامة الكبرى (al-imāmah al-kubrā): The greater imamate; the general political leadership of the Muslim community (caliphate).
الإمامة الصغرى (al-imāmah al-ṣughrā): The minor imamate; leading congregational prayer.
ربط صلاة المقتدي بصلاة الإمام (rabṭ ṣalāt al-muqtadī bi-ṣalāt al-imām): Connecting the follower's prayer to the imam's prayer, meaning the follower's prayer is valid only through following the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Personal and collective imamate
C) Fard and sunnah imamate
D) Male and female imamate

Key Takeaway
Imamate in Islamic law has two distinct meanings—caliphate and prayer leadership—each with its own conditions and rulings.

Facing the Qibla While Relieving Oneself: Prohibition or Permissibility?
Ruling on facing or turning back to the qibla in the privy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing or turning back to the qibla during elimination, explain the evidence, and evaluate the opposing view.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla while relieving oneself is prohibited (makruh tahrimi); the Prophet's action does not override the general command.

We now move from disliked actions in prayer to disliked actions outside prayer. The first issue is facing the qibla during elimination. While many assume it is merely disliked, the Hanafi school holds it is prohibited (tahriman). However, a report from Ibn Umar appears to contradict this. In this lesson, we examine the evidence and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi school holds that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibited dislike) to face the qibla with one's private parts or to turn one's back to the qibla while relieving oneself. This applies in both open spaces and built structures.
The term 'faraj' (private parts) applies to both men and women.
2
Identify the Hanafi dalil
The primary proof is the prophetic hadith: 'When you come to relieve yourselves, do not face the qibla nor turn your backs to it, but face east or west.' This is a general command (amr) indicating prohibition.
The hadith is general and includes all situations.
3
Identify the opposing view and its dalil
Some scholars (qil) argue it is not disliked, citing the hadith of Ibn Umar: he saw the Prophet relieving himself facing Syria with his back to the qibla. They interpret this as evidence of permissibility.
This opposing view is based on an action (fi'l) of the Prophet.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that a clear command (qawl) takes precedence over an action that may have been situation-specific. The action does not abrogate the command unless there is clear indication; here there is none, so the prohibition remains.
This is a key usul principle: qawl muqaddam 'ala al-fi'l.
5
Determine the practical effect (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, a Hanafi must avoid facing or turning back to the qibla. If one forgets and sits facing it, it is recommended to turn away as much as possible. The act is sinful but does not invalidate other acts.
Additional rulings: it is also disliked to point one's foot towards the qibla or towards a Mushaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [ أي هذا فصل في مسائل تتعلق بباب الكراهة لما فرغ من الأشياء المكروهة في الصلاة شرع في الأشياء المكروهة خارج الصلاة، وفصل بقوله: فصل. (مسكين) كره إلخ أي تحريماً، وهو بإطلاقه شامل لما لو كان ذيله ساقطاً على الأرض، وقيل: لا يكره، وعم إطلاقه الفضاء والبنيان؛ لإطلاق قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: 'إذا أتيتم الغائط فلا تستقبلوا القبلة ولا تستدبروها ولكن شرقوا أو غربوا'. و'الفرج' يعم قبل الرجل والمرأة باتفاق أهل اللغة. (فتح) في الخلاء بالمد هو بيت الخلاء، أي عند البول والغائط. (ع) واستدبارها وقيل لا يكره؛ لحديث ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما قال: 'رقيت يوماً على بيت أختي حفصة، فرأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قاعداً لحاجته مستقبل الشام مستدبر القبلة'، والأحوط الأول؛ لأن القول مقدم على الفعل، وإن غفل فجلس مستقبلاً يستحب له أن ينحرف بقدر الإمكان، وقالوا: يكره للمرأة إمساك الصبي نحو القبلة للبول، ويكره أيضاً مد الرجل إليها أو إلى المصحف أو كتب الفقه إلا أن يكون على مكان مرتفع من المحاذاة. (فتح)
Chapter: This chapter is on matters related to the section on disliked things. After finishing the disliked things in prayer, he began on the disliked things outside prayer, and he started with 'Chapter'. He said: 'It is disliked (i.e., prohibited) to face the qibla with the private parts in the privy and to turn one's back to it.' The meaning is that it is prohibited (tahriman). It generally includes even if his garment trail is touching the ground. And it was said: it is not disliked. And its generality includes open spaces and buildings due to the general nature of his saying: 'When you come to relieve yourselves, do not face the qibla nor turn your backs to it, but face east or west.' And 'al-faraj' encompasses the private parts of men and women by agreement of linguists. 'In the privy' (al-khala') with madd is the house of relieving oneself, i.e., at the time of urine and stool. And turning one's back to it: it was said that it is not disliked due to the hadith of Ibn Umar who said: 'I climbed onto the roof of my sister Hafsah's house and saw the Messenger of Allah sitting for his need facing Syria with his back to the qibla.' And the more precautionary is the first (i.e., to prohibit) because the saying (hadith) is given precedence over the action. If someone forgets and sits facing it, it is recommended for him to turn away as much as possible. They said: it is disliked for a woman to hold a boy facing the qibla for urination, and it is also disliked to extend one's leg towards the qibla or towards a Mushaf or books of fiqh unless it is on a high place away from direct alignment.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage introduces a new chapter on disliked actions outside of prayer, specifically regarding the qibla when relieving oneself. The main ruling is that it is prohibited (makruh tahrimi) to face the qibla or turn one's back to it while urinating or defecating. This includes both open spaces and built toilets. The basis is the prophetic hadith commanding not to face or turn back to the qibla. The term 'faraj' (private parts) applies to both men and women. There is a dissenting view based on a report from Ibn Umar that the Prophet was seen relieving himself facing Syria with his back to the qibla. However, the author states that the more precautionary view is the first, because the explicit command (the saying) is given precedence over an action that may have been for a specific reason. If one forgets and sits facing the qibla, it is recommended to turn as much as possible. Additional rulings: it is disliked for a woman to hold a boy facing the qibla for urination, and it is also disliked to point one's foot towards the qibla or towards a Mushaf or books of fiqh, unless the foot is on a high place that prevents direct alignment.

استدبار القبلة (istidbar al-qiblah): Turning one's back to the qibla when relieving oneself.
الخلاء (al-khala'): The privy or place of relieving oneself.

Key Takeaway
Facing or turning back to the qibla during elimination is prohibited (makruh tahrimi); if one forgets, turning away is recommended.

Obligation of Hastening and Prohibition of Selling at First Adhan
Ruling on hastening to Friday prayer and prohibition of selling after first adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sa'y (hastening to Friday prayer) is wajib and selling is prohibited at the first adhan after zawal, cite the Quranic evidence (al-Jumu'ah:9), and explain the intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab disputes regarding the timing.

Core Idea
The obligation to hasten to Friday prayer and the prohibition of selling begin with the first adhan after zawal—this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes a key ruling for Friday prayer: the moment the first adhan is called after noon (zawal) on Friday, it becomes wajib to proceed to the mosque and forbidden to engage in buying and selling. The author then discusses various opinions about which adhan triggers this obligation, citing the Quranic command and historical practice. Understanding this ruling is essential for every Muslim to align their Friday worship and commerce correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The text states it is wajib to hasten (sa'y) and to leave off selling (tark al-bay'). The hukm for sa'y is wajib; the command to leave selling is a prohibition (haram).
Note: The obligation is tied to the first adhan, not the second.
2
Locate the primary evidence (dalil)
The Quranic verse al-Jumu'ah:9 is cited. The imperative 'fas'aw' indicates obligation per Hanafi usul, and 'dharu al-bay'' indicates prohibition. However, the timing is linked to 'nudiya' (the call), which is interpreted as the first adhan.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala regarding the specific timing.
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab disputes
Several opinions exist: (1) first adhan after zawal (mufta bihi), (2) second adhan near pulpit, (3) entry of time regardless of adhan, (4) adhan on minaret from Abu Hanifa. Trace the basis for each.
The text says 'في الأصح' indicating the first view is preferred.
4
Examine the inter-madhhab dispute
Some Shafi'is and Hanbalis consider a sale contracted during the adhan as invalid (batil), while Hanafis hold it is valid but makruh. Understand the practical consequence (thamarah).
This difference arises from interpreting the command 'dharu al-bay'' as a prohibition of the contract itself vs. a prohibition of engaging in trade.
5
Apply the ruling to a real sale scenario
If a sale is contracted after the first adhan, the contract is valid but the act is disliked. The seller should have hastened to the mosque. The ruling applies to all forms of trade in the modern context, including e-commerce.
The ruling does not invalidate the contract; it only declares the timing inappropriate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة ويجب باب صلاة الجمعة السعي وترك البيع بالأذان الأول، فإن جلس على المنبر أذن بين يديه، على من عليه الجمعة إلى الجمعة بعد تمام وأقيم الخطبة. بإقامة الجمعة ولو مع السعي أي الإمام يعني أذن المؤذن بالأذان الأول: [الواقع بعد الزوال في الأصح. (ط)] وقيل: يجب السعي بالأذان الثاني أي عند المنبر؛ لأنه لم يكن في زمن النبي إلا هو، وكذا في عهد أبي بكر وعمر لها وزاد عثمان اهله الله الأذان على الزوراء أي المكان المرتفع، وقيل: يجب بدخول الوقت وإن لم يؤذن لها أحد، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن المعتبر في وجوب السعي وحرمة البيع الأذان على المنارة، والأصل في ذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿إِذَا نُودِيَ لِلصَّلاةِ مِنْ يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ وَذَرُوا الْبَيْعَ﴾ (الجمعة:٩) ثم إذا عقد البيع وقت الأذان ينعقد، ولكنه يكره خلافاً لبعض الشافعية والحنابلة رمز الحقائق: ۱۰۰/١](مستخلص) أذن إلخ بالبناء للمفعول ولا يستعمل مبنياً للفاعل، وقوله: "بين يديه" أي بين يدي الخطيب، وأفاد بوحدة الفعل أن المؤذن إن كان أكثر من واحد أذنوا واحداً بعد واحد يعني إذا اتسع المسجد وكثر الجماعات بحيث أن صوت المؤذن وحده لا يبلغ جميعهم واحتيج إلى اجتماع المؤذنين في الأذان لا يجتمعون، بل يؤذنون واحدا بعد واحد بأن يجعل كل مؤذن في ناحية من نواحي المسجد. (فتح) تتمة: لم يذكر المصنف الأمور المستحبة يوم الجمعة كما ذكرها في صلاة العيد فلنذكر شيئاً منها، فالمستحب لمن أراد حضور الجمعة أن يدهن وأن يمس طيبا، وأن يلبس أحسن ثيابه وأن تكون بيضا، وأن يقعد عند استماع الخطبة كما يقعد في التشهد ولا بأس بالاحتباء، وينبغي للإمام أن يقرأ فيها كالظهر، ولو قرأ تبركا بالسور المأثورة كان حسنا إن لم يواظب عليه، وأن يتبكر، وأن يجلس في الصف الأول إن قدر وهو ما يلي الإمام، ثم اعلم أنهم اختلفوا في جواز السؤال في المسجد وفي جواز الدفع إليه والمختار أن السائل إن كان لا يمر بين يدي المصلي ولا يتخطى رقاب الناس، ولا يسأل إلحافاً بل لأمر لابد منه، فلا بأس بالسؤال، والدفع إليه، ولا بأس الجمعة إذا خرج من عمران المصر قبل دخول وقت الظهر، والصحيح أنه يكره السفر بعد الزوال قبل أن يصليها. ولا يكره قبل الزوال. (فتح) بين يديه أي بين يدي المنبر، بذلك جرى التوارث، ولا ينبغي أن يصلي غير الخطيب؛ لأن القصر للخطبة فلا يقيمهما اثنان [ رمز الحقائق (١٠١/١] تمام الخطبة والفصل بينهما بأمر الدنيا مكروه.
The Book of Prayer. The Chapter of Friday Prayer. The obligation of hastening and leaving off selling at the first adhan. Then if he sits on the pulpit, the adhan is called in his presence. Upon whom Friday is obligatory, until the next Friday after the completion of the khutbah, and the iqamah for the Friday prayer is established, even with hastening. Meaning: the Imam, i.e., the muezzin calls the first adhan, which occurs after zawal in the correct view. And some say: hastening becomes obligatory with the second adhan, i.e., near the pulpit, because in the time of the Prophet there was only this, and similarly in the era of Abu Bakr and Umar. Uthman added the adhan on al-Zawra', i.e., a high place. And some say: it becomes obligatory at the entering of the time even if no one calls the adhan. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that the effective criterion in the obligation of hastening and the prohibition of selling is the adhan on the minaret. The basis for this is the saying of Allah Most High: 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off selling' (al-Jumu'ah:9). Then if a sale is contracted at the time of the adhan, it is concluded but it is disliked, contrary to some Shafi'is and Hanbalis. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 100/1, Mustakhlas). 'Adhan' etc. is in the passive voice and not used actively. His saying 'in his presence' means in the presence of the khatib. The unity of the verb indicates that if there is more than one muezzin, they call one after another. That is, if the mosque is spacious and the congregations are many such that the voice of one muezzin alone does not reach all of them and there is need for multiple muezzins, they do not all call together but call one after another, with each muezzin in a direction of the mosque. (Fath) A supplement: The author did not mention the recommended acts on Friday as he did for Eid prayer, so we will mention some: It is recommended for whoever intends to attend Friday to apply oil, apply perfume, wear his best clothes and that they be white, and to sit while listening to the khutbah as he sits in tashahhud, and there is no problem with ihtiba' (sitting on heels with knees drawn up). It is befitting for the Imam to recite as in zuhr, and if he recites the transmitted surahs seeking blessing, it is good as long as he does not persist. Also to go early, to sit in the first row if possible, which is the row closest to the Imam. Then know that they differed regarding the permissibility of asking in the mosque and giving to a beggar. The chosen view is that if the beggar does not pass in front of the worshippers, does not step over people's necks, and does not ask insistently but for a necessary need, then there is no harm in asking and giving. And it is permissible to leave the built-up area of the city before the entry of zuhr time. The correct view is that traveling after zawal before praying it is disliked, but not disliked before zawal. (Fath) 'In his presence' means near the pulpit; this is what has been inherited. And no one other than the khatib should lead the prayer because the qasr (shortening) is for the khutbah, so two should not deliver it. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 101/1) Completing the khutbah and separating between the two with worldly matters is disliked.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligation of hastening to Friday prayer and the prohibition of selling after the adhan. The author begins by stating that 'hastening and leaving off selling is obligatory at the first adhan.' This refers to the adhan that occurs after zuhr time enters. However, there is a dispute: some say the obligation is tied to the second adhan, which is the one called near the pulpit before the khutbah, as this was the practice in the Prophet's time and the era of the first two caliphs. Uthman added a third adhan on a raised place. Abu Hanifa, in a narration from al-Hasan, holds that the criterion is the adhan on the minaret. The proof is the Quranic verse: 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off selling.' The verse commands hastening and prohibits selling at the time of the call. If a sale is contracted during the adhan, it is valid but disliked, contrary to some Shafi'is and Hanbalis who consider it invalid. The passage then explains that 'adhan' is used in the passive voice, and the adhan is given near the khatib. If there are multiple muezzins, they should call one after another, not simultaneously, to ensure the call reaches everyone. The text then appends recommended acts for Friday: applying oil and perfume, wearing white clothes, sitting properly during the khutbah, going early, and sitting in the first row. It also discusses the permissibility of asking and giving in the mosque with conditions, and the ruling on traveling on Friday: it is disliked to travel after zawal before praying Friday, but not before zawal. Finally, it notes that only the khatib should lead the prayer, and it is disliked to separate between the two khutbahs with worldly talk.

Key Terms
السعي (al-sa'y): Hastening or proceeding to the Friday prayer; a wajib act.
الأذان الأول (al-adhan al-awwal): The first call to prayer on Friday, which occurs after the entry of zuhr time (after zawal).
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam before the Friday prayer; it is a condition (shart) for the validity of Friday prayer in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what triggers the obligation to hasten to Friday prayer and refrain from selling?
A) The first adhan after zawal
B) The second adhan near the pulpit
C) The entry of zuhr time
D) The appearance of the imam on the minbar

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the first adhan after zawal triggers the wajib of sa'y and the prohibition of selling; a sale contracted at that time is valid but disliked.

Recommended Acts and Other Rulings for Friday
Supplementary rulings on Friday: mustahabbat, travel, mosque etiquette, and khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least five recommended acts (mustahabbat) for Friday, state the ruling on traveling before and after zawal, and explain the etiquette of the khutbah and the conditions for permissibility of begging in the mosque.

Core Idea
Friday has many recommended acts; traveling after zawal is disliked, and only the khatib should lead the prayer.

After establishing the core obligations for Friday prayer, the text provides a valuable supplement on the sunnan (recommended acts) of Friday. These include applying oil, wearing perfume, wearing white clothes, sitting properly during the khutbah, going early, and sitting in the first row. It also addresses practical rulings on traveling, the permissibility of asking for and giving charity in the mosque, and that only the khatib should lead the prayer. Understanding these recommendations enhances one's Friday observance and avoids disliked practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts (mustahabbat)
List the actions recommended for Friday: applying oil, perfume, wearing best white clothes, sitting during khutbah like tashahhud, going early, sitting in first row, etc. These are not obligatory but carry reward.
These are mustahabbat, not wajib. The text says 'يستحب' (it is recommended).
2
Understand the etiquette of the khutbah
One should sit attentively during the khutbah. The text mentions sitting like in tashahhud, and that ihtiba' (sitting on heels with knees drawn up) is allowed. Also, the imam should recite as in zuhr, and it is disliked to separate the two khutbahs with worldly talk.
The khutbah is a condition (shart) for Friday prayer in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Assess the ruling on traveling on Friday
Traveling after zawal before performing Friday prayer is disliked (makruh). Traveling before zawal is not disliked. This applies to those upon whom Friday is obligatory.
The text says 'الصحيح أنه يكره السفر بعد الزوال قبل أن يصليها. ولا يكره قبل الزوال.'
4
Evaluate the permissibility of asking in the mosque
There is a difference of opinion. The chosen view (mukhtar) is that asking and giving are permissible if the beggar does not pass in front of worshippers, does not step over necks, and does not ask insistently, but for a genuine need.
This is a practical ruling for mosque etiquette.
5
Note the rule about who leads the prayer
Only the khatib should lead the Friday prayer. The text says 'ولا ينبغي أن يصلي غير الخطيب' (it is not proper for anyone other than the khatib to lead).
This is because the khutbah and prayer are connected; the same person should deliver both.

Key Terms
المستحب (al-mustahabb): Recommended act; doing it earns reward, leaving it is not sinful.
الاحتباء (al-ihtiba'): A sitting posture where one draws up knees and wraps arms around them.
الزوارء (al-Zawra'): A specific raised place in Medina where Uthman ordered the adhan to be called.

Rulings for the Dying Person: Positioning and Talqin
Opening chapter on funerals with rulings for the dying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for positioning the dying person towards the Qibla and prompting the shahada, explain the evidence, and distinguish the Hanafi position on post-burial talqin from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Turn dying person to Qibla on right side; prompt shahada before death; Hanafi: no talqin after burial.

This passage opens the chapter on funerals by addressing the final moments of life. The author presents two sunna actions for the person in the death throes: orienting him towards the Qibla and prompting him to utter the shahada. These actions are rooted in prophetic practice and aim to make the last words the testimony of faith. The text also introduces a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether prompting continues after burial. Our lesson will walk through these rulings, their proofs, and the practical difference between the schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sunna actions
Locate in the source the two recommended actions for the dying person: positioning towards the Qibla on the right side and prompting the shahada. Note that the matn states directly: 'المحتضر القبلة على يمينه، ولقن الشهادة'.
The matn is the core ruling; the commentary expands on the method.
2
Examine the evidence for talqin
Find the hadith cited in the commentary: 'من كان آخر كلامه لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة'. Understand that the Hanafi school uses this to support the recommendation (not obligation) of prompting, as it encourages the dying to end with the shahada.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its dalala is also zanni, hence the ruling is sunna, not wajib.
3
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation of 'your dead'
The hadith used by Shafi'i for post-burial talqin is 'لَقِّنُوا مَوْتَاكُمْ لا إِلَٰهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ'. Hanafi scholars interpret 'your dead' as those approaching death, not the already deceased, analogous to the phrase 'اقْرَؤُوا عَلَى مَوْتَاكُمْ يٰس' which refers to the dying.
This distinction is the crux of the ikhtilaf.
4
Compare with Shafi'i and identify the practical difference
Imam al-Shafi'i takes the hadith literally and recommends talqin after burial. The Hanafi response is that the dead are not addressed by commands; prompting after burial is not part of the sunna as transmitted in the zahir al-riwaya. The practical result: Hanafis do not prompt in the grave, Shafi'is do.
This thamarah al-khilaf is a concrete example of how usul differences affect practice.

أي وجه

المحتضر القبلة على يمينه، ولقن الشهادة، فإن مات شدّ .

أي المحتضر
باب الجنائز [جمع جنازة وهي بالفتح الميت وبالكسر : السرير الذي يحمل عليه الميت، من جنزت الشيء أجنزه إذا سترته. رمز الحقائق: ۱۰۷/۱۸] المناسبة بين هذا الباب وبين صلاة الخوف بل بين أبواب الصلاة أن صلاة الجنازة صلاة من وجه لا مطلقة بل متعلقة بعارض هو آخر ما يعرض للحي في دار التكليف؛ ولهذا أخرت عن الصلوات كلها، لكن المصنف أخر الصلاة في الكعبة ليكون ختم كتاب الصلاة بما يتبرك به حالاً ومكاناً، وأقحم لفظ "أحكام" إلى الجنازة، وقال: هي من إضافة الشيء إلى سببه؛ إذ الوجوب بحضور الجنازة أي وجوب جميع ما يتعلق بالميت من تغسيل وتكفين وصلاة وحمل ودفن بحضور الجنازة، والأحكام شاملة لجميعها. (فتح) المحتضر : يقال: احتضر على بناء المجهول إذا مات؛ لأن الوفاة أو ملائكة الموت حضرته، وعلامات الاحتضار: أن تسترخي قدماه، فلا ينتصبان وينعوج أنفه، وينخسف صدغاه، وتمتد جلدة الخصية؛ لأن الخصية تتعلق بالموت وتتدلي جلدها، ويستحب لأقربائه وجيرانه أن يدخلوا ويتلوا سورة "يس"، واستحسن بعض المتأخرين قراءة سورة الرعد، وينبغي إحضار الطيب ويخرج من عنده الجنب والحائض والنفساء، ومعنى "ولي القبلة" أي يوجه نحوها؛ لأنه عليه لما قدم المدينة سأل عن البراء بن معرور فقالوا: توفي وأوصى بثلث ماله لك، وأوصى أن : إلى القبلة لما احتضر، فقال علي: أصاب الفطرة - أي الإسلام - وقد رددت ثلثه على ولده" ثم ذهب فصلى
عليه. (فتح)
يوجه
على يمينه [ أي على شقه الأيمن، وإن شق عليه ترك على حاله. (ط، ع)] وهو السنة والمعتاد في زماننا أن يلقى على قفاه وقدماه إلى القبلة قالوا: لأنه أسهل لخروج الروح و لم يذكروا وجه ذلك، ولا يمكن معرفته إلا نقلا، ولكن يمكن أن يقال: هو أسهل لتغميضه وشد لحييه عقب الموت، ومنع من تقوس أعضائه ثم إذا ألقى على القفا يرفع رأسه قليلاً ليصير وجهه إلى القبلة دون السماء، والإضحاع للمريض أنواع: أحدها في الصلاة يستلقى على قفاه، والثاني في الموت يضجع على شقه الأيمن واختير الاستلقاء، والثالث في الصلاة عليه يضجع على قفاه معترضا القبلة، والرابع في اللحد يضجع على شقه الأيمن، ووجه إلى القبلة، هكذا توارث السنة. (فتح) ولقن الشهادة: المراد بالشهادة مجموع الشهادتين، ويلقن عند النزع قبل الغرغرة ولا يأمره بها، ويندب أن يكون الملقن غير متهم بالمسرة بموته، وأن يكون ممن يعتقد فيه الخير فيذكرها عنده جهرا عساه أن يأتي بها لتكون آخر كلامه؛ لقوله عليه: "من كان آخر كلامه لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة"؛ ولأنه موضع يتعرض فيه الشيطان لإفساد اعتقاده فيحتاج إلى مذكر ومنبه على التوحيد، ولو أتى بها مرة كفاه ولا يكثر عليه ما لم يتكلم بأجنبي، وهذا التلقين مستحب بالإجماع والتلقين على ثلاثة أوجه فللمحتضر لا خلاف في حسنه، وما بعد انقضاء مدة الدفن لا خلاف في عدم حسنه والثالث اختلفوا فيه وهو ما إذا تم دفنه وكيفيته أن يقول: يا فلان بن فلان اذكر
Chapter of Funerals. (Heading) The dying person: [turn him towards] the Qibla on his right side, and prompt him to [recite] the shahada. Then if he dies, tie [his jaws]. (Commentary) The chapter of funerals: plural of janaza, which with fatha means the deceased and with kasra means the bier on which the deceased is carried. The connection between this chapter and the chapter of the prayer of fear, rather between all chapters of prayer, is that the funeral prayer is a prayer in one sense, not absolute, but related to an incidental cause which is the last thing that happens to a living person in the abode of obligation; therefore it is delayed after all prayers. However, the author delayed the prayer in the Kaaba so that the book of prayer would conclude with what is blessed in state and place. He inserted the word 'rulings' to janaza and said: it is a genitive construction of the thing to its cause, since obligation arises from the presence of the janaza, i.e., obligation of all that pertains to the deceased from washing, shrouding, prayer, carrying, and burying due to the presence of the janaza, and the rulings encompass all of them. (Fath) Al-muhtadar: it is said: ihtadara on the passive pattern when he dies, because death or the angels of death attend him. Signs of the death throes: his feet become limp and cannot stand straight, his nose becomes crooked, his temples sink, and the skin of the scrotum stretches because the scrotum hangs at death and its skin dangles. It is recommended for his relatives and neighbors to enter and recite Surah Ya-Seen, and some later scholars considered reciting Surah Ar-Ra'd good. Perfume should be brought, and the junub, menstruating woman, and postpartum woman should leave. The meaning of 'turn him towards the Qibla' is that he is directed towards it, because when the Prophet (peace be upon him) came to Medina, he asked about Al-Bara' ibn Ma'rur. They said: He passed away, bequeathed a third of his wealth to you, and willed that he be turned towards the Qibla when he was dying. He (the Prophet) said: 'He hit the fitra (i.e., Islam), and I have returned his third to his children.' Then he went and prayed over him. (Fath) 'On his right side' i.e., on his right side; if it is difficult for him, leave him as he is. (T, A) And it is the sunna and the customary practice in our time that he is laid on his back with his feet towards the Qibla. They said: because it is easier for the soul to exit, but they did not mention the reason for that, and it cannot be known except by transmission. However, it can be said: it is easier for closing his eyes and tying his jaws after death, and to prevent curvature of his limbs. Then when he is laid on his back, his head is raised slightly so that his face is towards the Qibla, not towards the sky. The types of lying down for the sick: one in prayer: he lies on his back; second at death: he lies on his right side, but lying on the back is chosen; third in prayer over him: he lies on his back crosswise to the Qibla; fourth in the grave: he lies on his right side facing the Qibla. This is how the sunna has been transmitted. (Fath) 'And prompt him to the shahada': what is meant by shahada is the two testimonies together, and he is prompted at the time of death throes before the gurgling sound, and he is not commanded to say it. It is recommended that the prompter be not suspected of being pleased with his death, and that he be one in whom good is believed, so that he recites it audibly near him, hoping that he will utter it so that it becomes his last words, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever has as his last words 'la ilaha illa Allah' enters Paradise.' And because it is a place where Shaytan tries to corrupt his belief, so he needs a reminder and admonisher about tawhid. If he utters it once, that suffices, and he should not be made to repeat it unless he speaks something else. This talqin (prompting) is recommended by consensus. Talqin has three aspects: for the dying person, there is no disagreement about its goodness; after the completion of the burial period, there is no disagreement about its lack of goodness; and the third is disputed, which is when the burial is completed, and its manner is to say: 'O so-and-so son of so-and-so, remember...'
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on funerals (Bab al-Jana'iz). The author first defines key terms and explains the placement of this chapter after the prayer of fear and before prayer in the Kaaba, highlighting that funeral prayer is an attached act due to the incidental cause of death. The central ruling is for the dying person (muhtadar): he should be turned towards the Qibla on his right side, and if that is difficult, he may be left as is. The sunna method is to lay him on his back with feet towards the Qibla for ease of soul exit and post-death procedures. The text then details four types of lying positions for the sick. The second ruling is prompting (talqin) the shahada at the time of death before the gurgling sound, not commanding. The prompter should be a person of good standing. The evidence is the hadith: 'Whoever has as his last words la ilaha illa Allah enters Paradise.' The consensus confirms the recommendation. Talqin has three categories: during dying (agreed upon as good), after burial time (agreed upon as not good), and after burial is completed (disputed). The Hanafi position is that talqin is not recommended after burial, contrary to the Shafi'i view.

Key Terms
المحتضر (al-muhtadar): The person who is in the throes of death, on the verge of dying.
التلقين (al-talqin): Prompting the dying person to recite the shahada audibly so that it becomes his last words.
الشهادة (al-shahada): The two testimonies: 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh.'
الغرغرة (al-gharghara): The gurgling sound made by the dying person when the soul reaches the throat; after this point, talqin may not be effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when should the dying person be prompted to say the shahada?
A) Immediately after death
B) After burial
C) Before the gurgling sound (gharghara)
D) At any time before burial

Key Takeaway
The sunna for the dying is to face the Qibla (preferably on his back) and to be prompted with the shahada before death; the Hanafi school does not extend this prompting to after burial.

Initial Post-Death Actions: Sunna Practices and Obligatory Covering
Detailing sunna and wajib actions before washing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five sunna actions and the one wajib action in preparing the deceased, explain the evidence for covering and fumigation, and identify the Hanafi position on covering from navel to knee.

Core Idea
Covering the private parts of the deceased is wajib; all other initial actions are sunnah muakkadah to honor the dead.

After a Muslim dies, the community has a set of prescribed actions that must be performed before the ritual washing (ghusl). These actions, derived from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him), ensure the deceased is treated with dignity and respect. In this lesson, we explore the five sunna actions—tying the jaws, closing the eyes, fumigation of the bed, covering the private parts, and stripping the clothes—along with the evidence and the correct Hanafi view on the extent of covering. We also touch on supplementary practices and the dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding stripping.

Guided Path
1
List the acts and their hukm
Identify the five actions in the matn and determine which are sunnah and which is wajib. Refer to the text: tying jaws, closing eyes, fumigation, covering private parts, and stripping.
Covering is wajib; the rest are sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil for fumigation
Find the hadith cited: 'Allah is odd and loves odd numbers' (إن الله وتر يحب الوتر). Explain how it supports performing fumigation an odd number of times.
The dalil is ahad but accepted in practice.
3
Locate the dalil for covering
Find the hadith: 'Do not look at the thigh of a living or dead person' (لا تنظر إلى فخذ حي ولا ميت). Explain how it obligates covering the private parts because looking is prohibited.
The hadith implies covering is necessary.
4
Analyse the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on covering
Compare the two views: in the apparent riwaya, only the private parts (ghayridh) must be covered; in the nawadir, from navel to knee. State that the correct view (al-sahih) is the stricter covering from navel to knee.
This affects the minimum coverage required.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position on stripping
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the deceased should be washed in a shirt, while Hanafis insist on stripping (tajrid). Understand the Hanafi reasoning: to prevent rapid decay and allow thorough washing.
The Prophet's case is considered specific to him.

ما كنت عليه فقل: رضيت بالله ربا وبالإسلام دينا وبمحمد نبيا، وتلقين الميت في القبر مشروع عند أهل السنة؛ لأن الله تعالى يحييه في القبر، وقال الشافعي يلقن بعد الموت؛ لظاهر قوله عليه: "لقنوا موتاكم شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وعندنا في ظاهر الرواية: لا يلقن والمراد بموتاكم" في الحديث من قرب من الموت كما في اقرؤوها على موتاكم". (فتح) عيناه: تحسيناً له، ويوضع على بطنه حديدة؛ لئلا ينتفخ، كذا روي عن الشعبي. (ع) على سرير: وهو الذي يغسله عليه، فإن لم يوجد فعلى لوح أو حجر مرتفع ليمكن غسله وتقليبه. [رمز الحقائق: ۱۰۷/۱] مجمر: أي مبخر بعود ونحوه ؛ لإزالة الرائحة الكريهة. التخت
The manner of preparing the deceased: [tie] his jaws, close his eyes, place him on a fumigated bed an odd number of times, cover his private parts, remove his clothes, and perform [like] a legal ablution. (Commentary) ... [Details on each action: tying jaws with a cloth, closing eyes, placing on a bed that is fumigated odd times, covering private parts from navel to knee, removing clothes so they can clean him, performing wudu]. Appendices: When a Muslim dies, his limbs are stretched, and a sword or mirror is placed on his stomach; his right hand is placed on his right side and left on left; it is not permissible to place hands on the chest of the deceased as the disbelievers do; there is no harm in announcing his death to increase the congregation for prayer and seeking forgiveness, provided it is not with boastful praise. The commentary also explains the ruling on covering the private parts: it is obligatory, and the strict covering is from navel to knee in the apparent riwaya, but in the nawadir it is the same as the living. The deceased is stripped to allow washing, contrary to the Shafi'i view that he be washed in his shirt.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage details the sunna and recommended actions to be performed immediately after the death of a Muslim, before washing. The text lists five actions: (1) tying the jaws (lahyayn) with a cloth to prevent the mouth from gaping, (2) closing the eyes to improve appearance and prevent insects from entering, (3) placing the body on a bed or elevated surface that is fumigated with incense an odd number of times (once, three, or five) to remove odors, (4) covering the private parts (from navel to knee) as it is obligatory and unlawful to look at them, and (5) removing the clothes (tajrid) so the body can be washed, followed by performing a complete ablution (wudu) similar to that for prayer. The text includes a supplement (tatimma) with additional practices: stretching the limbs, placing a sword or mirror on the stomach to prevent bloating, placing the right hand on the right side and left on the left, and prohibiting placing the hands on the chest (a practice of disbelievers). It also permits announcing the death for the sake of increasing the congregation, provided it is not a boastful announcement. The passage also addresses the difference with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding stripping the deceased: Hanafis insist on stripping (except what is necessary for covering) to prevent rapid decay due to heat, while Shafi'is maintain that the deceased should be washed in his shirt as the Prophet was. The commentary notes that the strict covering (from navel to knee) is the correct view, consistent with the living.

Key Terms
اللحيان (al-lahyayan): The two jaws; the area where the beard grows.
المجمر (al-mijmar): An incense burner or fumigation apparatus used to perfume the bed of the deceased.
التجريد (al-tajrid): Stripping the deceased of his clothes before washing, leaving only the covering for private parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence for fumigating the bed an odd number of times?
A) A Quranic verse
B) The hadith 'Allah is odd and loves odd numbers'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy with the living

Key Takeaway
The initial post-death actions are sunna except covering the private parts from navel to knee, which is wajib; stripping the deceased is necessary for washing.
