Hanafi Ruling on Washing Martyrs: Categories and Dispute with al-Shafi'i
States the Hanafi ruling on washing martyrs and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing and praying over four categories of deceased Muslims and explain the proof from the practice of Ali (RA) used in the dispute with al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Martyrs killed unjustly are not washed; those killed by hadd/qisas are washed; rebels and highway robbers are not—all based on Ali's practice.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the Hanafi position on which categories of deceased Muslims are to be washed and have the funeral prayer performed. The text distinguishes four scenarios and engages in a dispute with al-Shafi'i, citing the practice of Sayyiduna Ali (RA) as a key proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
From the text, list the four types of deceased Muslims mentioned: 1) killed unjustly (zulman), 2) killed by hadd punishment, 3) killed by qisas/retaliation, 4) killed for rebellion or highway robbery. Note the ruling for each.
2
State the Hanafi position for each category
According to Hanafi school, those killed unjustly (martyrs in the specific sense) are NOT washed or prayed over. Those killed by hadd or qisas ARE washed and prayed over. Those killed for rebellion or highway robbery are NOT washed or prayed over.
The text explicitly excludes rebels and highway robbers from being washed.
3
Identify the opposing school and its position
Al-Shafi'i disagrees: he holds that any Muslim killed by right (including rebels) should be washed and prayed over, because he is still a Muslim.
The Shafi'i position treats all categories equally.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi evidence is the practice of Sayyiduna Ali (RA) who did not wash or pray over the Kharijites of Nahrawan, calling them 'our brothers who rebelled against us.' This indicates that rebellion (baghy) is the effective cause for not washing.
The Hanafi also analogize rebels to harbi (combatant) because they are waging war against Muslims.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in the Hanafi school, rebels are denied washing and prayer as a form of dishonor and deterrence; in the Shafi'i school, they receive the same treatment as any other deceased Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهيد
ظلماً أو قتل بحد أو قود، لا لبغي وقطع طريق. أي لا يغسل من قتل ظلماً أو قتل بحد أو قود: فإنه يغسل؛ لأنه ليس بمقتول ظلماً؛ لأنه بذل نفسه لإيفاء حق مستحق، ومن كان كذلك لم يكن في معنى شهداء أحد؛ لأنهم بذلوا أنفسهم لابتغاء مرضاة الله تعالى، فلا يلحق بهم. (مستخلص) بحد بأن كان محسناً فزنى فرجم ومات. [رمز الحقائق: ١١٤/١] أو قود: أي لأجل قصاص بأن قتل شخصاً فقتل مكانه أو تعزير؛ لأنه لم يقتل ظلما، فلا يكون شهيدا. (ط،ع) لا لبغي إلخ [ أي لأجل البغي وخروج عن طاعة الإمام] عطف على "حد"، والمعنى أنه يغسل من قتل بحد، لا لبغي وقطع طريق، فإنه لا يغسل إهانة، وكذا لا يصلى عليه إهانة وزجراً لغيره، وقال الشافعي: يغسل ويصلى عليه؛ لأنه مسلم، قتل بالحق، فصار كمن قتل بالقصاص، أو بالحد ولنا أن علياً رضي الله عنه لم يصل على أهل النهروان، أي الخوارج ولم يغسلهم، فقيل له: أهم كفار ؟ فقال : إخواننا بغوا علينا فأشار إلى العلة، وهو البغي؛ ولأنه قتل ظالماً لنفسه محارباً للمسلم كالحربي، فلا يغسل ولا يصلى عليه، وكذا من يقتل بالخنق غيلة. (فتح)
Chapter of the Martyr. [He is not washed if killed] unjustly or killed by hadd or qisas, not [if killed] for rebellion or highway robbery. That is, he is not washed who is killed unjustly or killed by hadd or qisas: indeed he is washed because he is not killed unjustly; because he gave himself for fulfillment of an established right, and one who is like that is not in the meaning of the martyrs of Uhud; because they gave themselves seeking the pleasure of Allah Almighty, so he is not attached to them. (Extracted) By hadd: such as he was a muhsin and committed zina so he was stoned and died. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 114/1] Or qisas: meaning for retaliation, such as he killed a person so he was killed in his place, or ta'zir; because he was not killed unjustly, so he is not a martyr. (T, A) 'Not for rebellion etc.' [meaning for rebellion and disobedience to the imam] is conjuncted to 'hadd', and the meaning is that one killed by hadd is washed, not one killed for rebellion and highway robbery, for he is not washed as dishonor, and likewise no prayer is performed over him as dishonor and deterrence for others. Al-Shafi'i said: he is washed and prayer is performed over him because he is a Muslim, killed by right, so he becomes like one killed by retaliation or by hadd. Our evidence: that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) did not pray over the people of Nahrawan, i.e., the Kharijites, and did not wash them. It was said to him: 'Are they disbelievers?' He said: 'Our brothers rebelled against us,' indicating the effective cause, which is rebellion. And because he is killed while being unjust to himself, waging war against Muslims like a harbi, so he is not washed and no prayer is performed over him. Likewise, one killed by strangulation treacherously. (Fath)
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq begins the chapter on the martyr (Bāb al-Shahīd). The passage type is an inter-madhhab dispute with proofs. The author states the Hanafi ruling: a martyr killed unjustly (zulman) is not washed, nor is the funeral prayer performed over him. However, if a Muslim is killed by a prescribed punishment (hadd) such as stoning for adultery, or by retaliation (qisas or qawad) for murder, then he is washed and the prayer is performed, because he gave himself up for a just right and is not considered a martyr in the sense of the Uhud martyrs who sought Allah's pleasure. Similarly, those killed for rebellion (baghy) or highway robbery (qat' al-tariq) are not washed, as a form of humiliation and deterrence. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that since such a person is a Muslim killed by right, he should be washed like one killed by qisas. The Hanafi response cites the practice of Sayyiduna Ali (RA) who did not wash or pray over the Kharijites of Nahrawan, explaining that their rebellion made them akin to combatants (harbi). The same applies to those killed treacherously by strangulation.

Key Terms
شهيد (shahīd): A martyr killed unjustly (zulman) in battle against disbelievers; such a person is not washed and no prayer is performed.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law, such as stoning for adultery. One killed by hadd is washed and prayed over.
قود (qawad): Retaliation (qisas) for murder. One killed by qisas is washed and prayed over.
بغي (baghy): Rebellion against the legitimate ruler. One killed for rebellion is not washed or prayed over.
قطع طريق (qat' al-tariq): Highway robbery. One killed for this crime is not washed or prayed over.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is washed and the funeral prayer is performed?
A) A Muslim killed unjustly in battle against disbelievers.
B) A Muslim executed by hadd punishment for zina.
C) A Muslim killed for rebellion (baghy).
D) A Muslim killed by highway robbers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between types of killing: those killed unjustly (martyrs) and rebels are not washed; those executed by hadd or qisas are washed.

I'tikaf: Definition, Ruling, and Conditions in the Hanafi School
Definition, ruling, and conditions of i'tikaf with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition and ruling of i'tikaf in the Hanafi school, identify its conditions, and explain the dispute regarding fasting as a condition.

Core Idea
I'tikaf's rukn is staying in a mosque with intention; fasting is condition for obligatory but not voluntary i'tikaf.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi ruling on i'tikaf, from its lexical meaning to its legal classification, conditions, and the scholarly debate on whether fasting is required. You will learn how the school distinguishes between obligatory, sunnah, and mustahabb i'tikaf, and why the condition of fasting differs by type.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition and rukn
Extract the lexical origin and the technical meaning of i'tikaf. Identify the rukn (pillar) – lubth (remaining) – and note that intention and mosque are conditions.
The rukn is minimal; without lubth there is no i'tikaf.
2
Classify the ruling (hukm level)
Determine the legal status: sunnah mu'akkadah kifayah for the last ten days of Ramadan, obligatory when vowed, mustahabb otherwise. Understand the consensus on sunnah kifayah.
The Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) is evidence for sunniyyah.
3
Distinguish conditions (shurut) and requirements
List the conditions: mosque (masjid jama'ah), intention, sanity, Islam. Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the type of mosque required.
Fasting is a condition only for obligatory (mandhur) i'tikaf, not for nafl in Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Analyze the fasting dispute
Compare the Hanafi position (fasting condition for wajib) with the Shafi'i view (fasting never a condition). Examine the evidence: hadith 'La i'tikafa illa bi al-sawm' vs. 'Laysa ala al-mu'takif sawm'. Understand the Hanafi response and the intra-Hanafi difference on nafl.
The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: fasting not condition for nafl; minimum is any duration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاعتكاف
سن لبث في مسجد بصوم ونيّة .
سنة
باب الاعتكاف
أي في بيان حكمه
ومنه
باب الاعتكاف يقال: من عكف أي أقبل على الشيء وأقام به واللازم يجيء من "نصر" ومصدره العكوف ومنه يَعْكُفُونَ عَلَى أَصْنَامٍ لَهُم الله (الأعراف: ۱۳۸) والمتعدي بمعنى الحبس من باب "ضرب" ومصدره العكف، وَالْهَدْيَ مَعْكوفا (الفتح: (٢٥) وهو من الشرائع القديمة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ أَنْ طَهِّرَا بَيْتِيَ لِلطَّائِفِينَ وَالْعَاكِفِينَ﴾ (البقرة:١٢٥) ولما كان الصوم شرطاً في بعض الاعتكاف أخره عنه. . (فتح) لبث: بفتح اللام وضمها وهو خبر محذوف ويجوز أن يكون نائب الفاعل والأول أولى، ثم اعلم أن الاعتكاف مؤ كدة إلا أنه سنة كفاية بالإجماع على عدم ملامة بعض أهل بلد إذا أتى به بعض منهم في العشر الأخير من رمضان وقيل مستحب، والصحيح أنه سنة مؤكدة للمواظبة عليه في العشر الأخير وهي دليل السنية، والحق أنه ينقسم إلى واجب وهو المنذور، وسنة وهو في العشر الأخير من رمضان، ومستحب في غيره من الأزمنة، ومن محاسن الاعتكاف تفريغ القلب من أمور الدنيا وتسليم النفس للمولى، وملازمة عبادته وبيته، وأما اعتكاف العشر الأوسط فقد ورد أنه عليه اعتكفه، فلما فرغ أتاه جبريل علي، فقال: إن الذي تطلبه أمامك يعني ليلة القدر فاعتكف العشر الأخير، وعن هذا ذهب الأكثر إلى أنها في العشر الأخير من رمضان، فمنهم من قال: في ليلة إحدى وعشرين ومنهم من قال في ليلة سبع وعشرين وقيل غير ذلك ثم ركن الاعتكاف هو اللبث، والمسجد والنية شرطان ولا خفاء أن صحتها تتوقف على العقل والإسلام فلا حاجة لذكرهما في الشروط، ومن الشروط أن يكون في مسجد جماعة أي مسجد تؤدى فيه بعض الصلوات.
وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال كل مسجد له إمام ومؤذن معلوم، وتؤدى فيه الصلوات الخمس بجماعة، وعن أبي يوسف أن الاعتكاف الواجب لا يجوز في مسجد غير جماعة، وغير الواجب يجوز في غيره، ثم الصوم شرط لصحة الاعتكاف الواجب؛ لحديث عائشة لما قالت: "السنة على المعتكف أن لا يعود مريضاً ولا يشهد جنازة ولا يمس امرأة ولا يباشرها ولا يخرج إلا لما لابد منه، ولا اعتكاف إلا بالصوم ولا اعتكاف إلا في مسجد جامع" ومثله لا يعرف إلا سماعا، ولم يرو أنه عليه اعتكف بغير صوم ولو كان جائزاً لفعل تعليماً، وقال الشافعي: الصوم ليس بشرط بقول على ه: ليس على المعتكف صوم إلا أن يوجبه على نفسه، ولنا قوله علية: "لا اعتكاف إلا بالصوم وما رواه أثر فلا يعارض الخبر، ولئن سلمنا المعارضة فنقول: هو محمول على غير المنذور بدليل قوله: "إلا أن يوجبه على نفسه" ، واختلفت الروايات في النفل، فروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن الصوم شرط لصحته، فعلى هذا لا يكون أقل من يوم وفي ظاهر الرواية ليس بشرط وهو قولهما، فيكون أقله ساعة بلا صوم، وليس لأقله تقدير، حتى لو دخل المسجد بنية الاعتكاف فهو معتكف ما أقام وتارك له إذا خرج، ثم أفضل الاعتكاف ما يكون في المسجد الحرام، ثم في مسجد النبي له أي الذي كان في زمنه لا ما زيد عليه، ثم في بيت المقدس، ثم في الجامع، ثم في كل مسجد أهله أكثر . (مسكين، فتح عيني) في مسجد: متعلق بقوله: لبث ونية عطف عليه. (ع)
Chapter of I'tikaf
It is a sunnah to remain in a mosque with fasting and intention.
Sunnah
Chapter of I'tikaf
Meaning: in explaining its ruling. And from it: Chapter of I'tikaf. It is said: from 'akafa, meaning he inclined towards something and remained with it. The intransitive comes from the pattern 'nasara' and its verbal noun is 'al-ukuf', and from it [the verse] {They remain devoted to their idols} (al-A'raf:138). The transitive verb meaning 'to detain' comes from the pattern 'daraba' and its verbal noun is 'al-akf', and [the verse] {And the sacrificial animals detained} (al-Fath:25). It is from the ancient legislations; due to His statement: {Purify My House for those who perform tawaf and those who stay in i'tikaf} (al-Baqarah:125). And since fasting is a condition in some i'tikaf, he (the author) delayed it after it. (Fath) 'Lubth' (remaining): with fatha on lam or damma, it is a deleted predicate, and it is possible that it is the deputy subject, and the first is more appropriate. Then know that i'tikaf is emphasized, but it is a sunnah kifayah by consensus that no blame falls upon some people of a town if some of them perform it in the last ten days of Ramadan. It was said it is mustahabb, and the correct view is that it is an emphasized sunnah due to persistent practice in the last ten days, and that is the evidence of sunniyyah. The truth is that it divides into: obligatory (mandhur), sunnah (in the last ten days of Ramadan), and mustahabb (at other times). Among the merits of i'tikaf is emptying the heart from worldly matters and submitting the soul to the Lord, and clinging to His worship and His house. As for the i'tikaf of the middle ten days, it has been related that the Prophet (peace be upon him) observed it; when he finished, Jibreel came to him and said: 'That which you seek is before you' meaning Laylat al-Qadr, so he observed i'tikaf in the last ten days. Based on this, the majority held that it is in the last ten days of Ramadan; some said on the twenty-first night, some said on the twenty-seventh night, and other opinions. Then the pillar (rukn) of i'tikaf is remaining (lubth), and the mosque and intention are conditions. It is obvious that its validity depends on sanity and Islam, so there is no need to mention them among the conditions. Among the conditions is that it be in a mosque of congregation, i.e., a mosque in which some prayers are performed.
And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: 'Every mosque that has a known imam and muezzin, and the five prayers are performed in congregation.' And from Abu Yusuf that obligatory i'tikaf is not valid in a non-congregation mosque, but non-obligatory is valid elsewhere. Then fasting is a condition for the validity of obligatory i'tikaf; due to the hadith of Aisha when she said: 'The sunnah for the one in i'tikaf is not to visit a sick person, nor attend a funeral, nor touch a woman, nor have intercourse, nor leave except for what is unavoidable, and no i'tikaf except with fasting, and no i'tikaf except in a congregational mosque.' Such a thing is not known except by hearing. And it is not narrated that he (peace be upon him) performed i'tikaf without fasting; if it were permissible he would have done so to teach. Al-Shafi'i said: 'Fasting is not a condition' based on his statement: 'There is no fasting upon the one in i'tikaf unless he makes it obligatory upon himself.' Our proof is his (peace be upon him) statement: 'No i'tikaf except with fasting.' What he narrated (i.e., the athar) does not contradict the khabar. And if we concede contradiction, we say: it is interpreted as non-obligatory (i'tikaf) due to his statement: 'unless he makes it obligatory upon himself.' And there is difference of narration regarding supererogatory (nafl). Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that fasting is a condition for its validity; accordingly it cannot be less than a day. In the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), it is not a condition, and it is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Thus its minimum is an hour without fasting, and there is no fixed limit for its minimum; so if one enters the mosque with the intention of i'tikaf, he is in i'tikaf as long as he remains and leaves it when he exits. Then the most excellent i'tikaf is in the Sacred Mosque, then in the Mosque of the Prophet (peace be upon him) i.e., that which existed in his time, not what was added to it, then in Bayt al-Maqdis, then in the congregational mosque (jami'), then in every mosque whose people are more numerous. (Miskin, Fath 'Ayni) 'Fi masjid' (in a mosque): related to his statement 'lubth' (remaining), and 'niyyah' (intention) is conjoined to it. (Aini)
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on i'tikaf from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It provides a lexical and legal definition, the ruling, and key conditions. The passage type is a definition with ruling and intra- and inter-madhhab disputes.  The author begins by stating that i'tikaf is 'sunnah' – remaining in a mosque with fasting and intention. The commentator (Fath) explains that 'lubth' (remaining) is the subject of a deleted predicate. The ruling: i'tikaf is a sunnah kifayah (communal sunnah) – if some people perform it, the obligation is lifted from the community. It is emphatically sunnah in the last ten days of Ramadan due to the Prophet's constant practice. However, the ruling is not monolithic: it divides into obligatory (mandhur), sunnah (last ten days), and mustahabb (other times). The rukn (pillar) is the remaining (lubth) in the mosque with intention – these are the essential elements. Conditions include the mosque being a masjid jama'ah (congregational mosque) where prayers are held. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa (in a narration from al-Hasan) requires a mosque with a known imam and muezzin and all five prayers; Abu Yusuf says obligatory i'tikaf requires a congregational mosque but voluntary may be elsewhere.  The core dispute in this passage is whether fasting is a condition for i'tikaf. The Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that fasting is a condition for obligatory (mandhur) i'tikaf based on the hadith 'La i'tikafa illa bi al-sawm' (No i'tikaf except with fasting) and the practice of the Prophet. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, saying fasting is not a condition, citing the hadith 'Not upon the one in i'tikaf is fasting unless he obligates it on himself.' The Hanafi response: the Shafi'i's athar does not contradict the stronger khabar; and if there is a conflict, the Shafi'i's hadith is interpreted as referring to voluntary i'tikaf, due to the phrase 'unless he obligates it on himself'. For nafl i'tikaf, there is difference within the Hanafi school: al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa says fasting is required, thus a minimum of one day; but in Zahir al-Riwayah (the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), fasting is not a condition, so the minimum is any duration, even an hour. The best i'tikaf is in the Haram, then the Prophet's mosque (original boundaries), then al-Aqsa, then the jami', then any mosque with larger congregation.

Key Terms
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): Remaining in a mosque with intention for worship, with or without fasting depending on type.
اللبث (al-lubth): The pillar (rukn) of i'tikaf – staying in the mosque.
سنة كفاية (sunnah kifayah): A recommended act that if performed by some, the obligation is lifted from the rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Which of the following is NOT a condition for i'tikaf according to the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah)?
A) Intention (niyyah)
B) Fasting for nafl i'tikaf
C) Being in a mosque
D) Sanity

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf is a sunnah kifayah in the last ten days of Ramadan; its validity requires remaining in a mosque with intention; fasting is required only for obligatory i'tikaf.

Permissible Exits from I'tikaf: Natural and Religious Needs
Lists prohibitions, valid reasons for leaving, and disputes on Friday exit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of permissible exits from i'tikaf (natural and religious), apply the Hanafi ruling that leaving for Friday prayer is permitted, and distinguish the effect of leaving without excuse on obligatory vs. nafl i'tikaf.

Core Idea
Leaving the mosque for a genuine natural or religious need does not invalidate i'tikaf.

The mu'takif is bound to remain in the mosque, but Islam recognizes that certain needs require leaving. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains which exits are permitted and which invalidate i'tikaf. It also addresses a key dispute: does attending Friday prayer preserve the validity of i'tikaf? Understanding these exceptions is crucial for anyone undertaking this sunnah worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
I'tikaf is a sunnah act (or wajib if vowed). The prohibited act is leaving the mosque without a valid excuse. The passage outlines the exceptions.
Distinguish between obligatory (by vow) and nafl i'tikaf regarding consequences.
2
Understand the two permissible categories
Hajah tabi'iyyah (natural) includes urination, defecation, ghusl for janabah. Hajah shar'iyyah (religious) includes Friday prayer and adhan from outside the mosque.
These are the only reasons that permit leaving.
3
Examine the dalil for natural need
The hadith of Aisha states the Prophet (peace be upon him) only left for 'human need'. This establishes the exception for unavoidable natural needs.
The exception is limited to the necessity; one must return promptly.
4
Analyze the dispute on Friday prayer
Hanafis permit leaving for Friday because i'tikaf in any mosque is valid (Quran 2:187) and Friday attendance is obligatory (Quran 62:9). Shafi'i and Malik argue one could have chosen a central mosque, so no necessity exists.
The Hanafi view is mufta bihi.
5
Distinguish between obligatory and nafl i'tikaf
Leaving without excuse invalidates obligatory i'tikaf (requires qada). For nafl, it simply ends – no qada required. Also note the disagreement among the Sahibayn on the threshold for nafl.
Muhammad says any exit invalidates; Abu Yusuf says only if more than half a day.

Prohibitions of I'tikaf
And its minimum as a nafl is an hour. And a woman performs i'tikaf in the mosque of her house (prayer area) and does not leave except for a religious need
from the mosque
like Friday prayer, or a natural need like urination and defecation. If he leaves for an hour without an excuse, it becomes invalid.
and the two 'Eids
from the mosque, temporal not spatial
his i'tikaf according to Abu Hanifa
'Nafl' is in the accusative as a state: i.e., the minimum of i'tikaf when it is nafl. (Aini) 'an hour' according to Muhammad; according to Abu Yusuf: most of the day; according to Imam (Abu Hanifa): a day. (Tahawi) 'Fi masjid' (in a mosque): this is the definition of i'tikaf legally: it is remaining in a mosque with fasting and intention. The linguistic meaning is present in it with an addition. And what is meant is the mosque in which congregation for the five prayers is held. (Tahawi, Aini) 'Fi masjid baytiha' (in the mosque of her house): it is the place she has prepared for prayer in her house. If she performs i'tikaf in the mosque, it is permissible but disliked (makruh). (Tahawi)] This is a statement of preference; therefore, if she performs i'tikaf in the mosque, it is permissible with karahah. If there is no prayer place in her house, i'tikaf is not valid there. And she does not leave her house when in i'tikaf without an excuse; if she leaves without an excuse, it becomes invalid. This applies to obligatory (by vow). As for nafl, it does not become invalid but ends. And her i'tikaf in the mosque of her house is because it is more protective for her. According to the three (Imams other than Hanafi? or the Sahibayn?), it is not permissible for her to do that; rather she performs i'tikaf in any mosque other than the mosque of her house. (Aini, Fath)
And he does not leave — i.e., it is not permissible for the mu'takif to leave his place of i'tikaf except for a need, which is of two types: religious and natural. As for leaving for a natural need: based on the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would not leave his i'tikaf except for human need. And because it is known that it occurs, so leaving to fulfill it is necessary. Thus leaving for it is exempted from the requirement of the pillar, which is remaining. However, he should not stay after completing his purification, because what is established by necessity is limited to its extent.
As for a religious need such as Friday prayer and the adhan if the minaret is outside the mosque: it is permissible for him to leave according to us. Al-Shafi'i and Malik said: Leaving for Friday invalidates it, because there is no necessity for him since he can perform i'tikaf in the central mosque (jami'). We say: I'tikaf in every mosque is legislated due to His statement: {while you are staying in the mosques} (al-Baqarah:187), which includes all. Then he is commanded to hasten to it (Friday prayer) due to His statement: {so hasten} (al-Jumu'ah:9). Thus leaving for it is exempted like for human need. So if starting i'tikaf in a mosque is valid, the necessity is established. He leaves for Friday when the sun declines (zawal), and from his i'tikaf place he leaves at a time to catch it with its sunnah, and after it with its sunnah, either four or six rak'ahs. If he stays longer, it does not invalidate because it is a place for him; but it is disliked (makruh tanzihan) due to opposing what he committed himself to without necessity. (Fath, Mustakhlis) Or natural need: what is unavoidable and what cannot be fulfilled in the mosque. (Miskin) And defecation and bathing if he has a wet dream and cannot bathe in the mosque. (Tahawi) Without a legitimate excuse, such as collapse of the mosque, or dispersal of its people, or natural like fear for his life or property, not visiting a sick person or attending a funeral (Tahawi, Aini). It becomes invalid: because i'tikaf is remaining, and leaving contradicts it, thus it nullifies it, whether the leaving is little or much, and he must make it up. What is meant by leaving is the separation of both feet from the mosque, to exclude if he puts his head out into his house, that does not invalidate his i'tikaf. Then the invalidation by leaving without an excuse is restricted to obligatory (wajib); as for nafl, it does not invalidate even without excuse as in al-Majma'. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It does not invalidate unless he leaves more than half a day, because if a little were not permitted, hardship would occur; because the mu'takif when he leaves for human need is not commanded to hurry in walking.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage details the prohibitions (muhdharat) of i'tikaf and the permissible exits. The passage type is a ruling with proof and dispute. It begins by stating the minimum duration for nafl i'tikaf: an hour according to Muhammad, most of the day according to Abu Yusuf, and one day according to Abu Hanifa. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Then it discusses women's i'tikaf: a woman's i'tikaf is preferably in her designated prayer area at home (masjid baytiha) because it is safer. It is permissible for her to do i'tikaf in a mosque but disliked. If she leaves without excuse, it invalidates obligatory i'tikaf, but for nafl it simply ends (does not require qada). The three (Imams Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad?) hold that a woman cannot do i'tikaf at home; she must be in a mosque.  The core ruling: the mu'takif may not leave the mosque except for two types of need: shar'iyyah (religious) like Friday prayer and adhan (if minaret is outside), and tabi'iyyah (natural) like urination, defecation, or ghusl if janabah and cannot bathe in the mosque. The hadith of Aisha is cited: the Prophet only left for 'human need'. Unnecessary exit invalidates obligatory i'tikaf. There is a dispute regarding leaving for Friday prayer: Hanafis permit it because i'tikaf in any mosque is valid, and Friday obligation takes precedence. Shafi'i and Malik consider it invalidating because one could have chosen a jami' mosque. The Hanafi response: the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 187) permits i'tikaf in all mosques, and the command to hasten to Jumu'ah (al-Jumu'ah 9) creates an exception. If the mu'takif leaves for Friday, he may pray the sunnah before and after (four or six rak'ahs) without invalidation, though staying longer is makruh tanzihi.  Natural needs are any unavoidable acts that cannot be done in the mosque. Leaving without any excuse invalidates obligatory i'tikaf immediately once both feet leave the mosque. For nafl i'tikaf, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn?) differ: Imam Muhammad holds that any exit without excuse invalidates; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (in one narration) say it only invalidates if more than half a day. The text ends mid-sentence noting that if leaving for human need, the mu'takif is not required to rush.

Key Terms
محظورات الاعتكاف (muhdharat al-i'tikaf): Actions prohibited during i'tikaf, primarily leaving the mosque without valid excuse.
حاجة شرعية (hajah shar'iyyah): A religiously recognized need that permits leaving the mosque, such as Friday prayer or adhan from outside minaret.
حاجة طبيعية (hajah tabi'iyyah): A natural physical need that cannot be fulfilled inside the mosque, like urination, defecation, or ghusl for janabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person in obligatory i'tikaf leaves the mosque to attend Friday prayer, what is the ruling?
A) The i'tikaf becomes invalid and must be restarted
B) The i'tikaf remains valid; leaving is permissible
C) It is permissible only if he stays less than an hour
D) It is permissible only if he prays nothing else

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque for a valid religious or natural need does not invalidate i'tikaf; the obligation of Friday prayer provides a legitimate religious need.

Taharah — Purification

Conditions for Fosterage Prohibition: The Principle of Predominance (Ghalaba)
Defines fosterage mahram relations and rules for mixing milk with other substances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for fosterage prohibition when milk is mixed with other substances, and apply the principle of predominance (ghalaba) to determine mahram relations.

Core Idea
A mixture only fosters if milk is predominant and nourishes growth.

Fosterage (rada') creates permanent marriage prohibitions, but not every trace of milk suffices. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rule that the milk must be predominant (ghalib) and capable of causing growth. You will learn the definitions, the intra-Hanafi differences, and the proof from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify Basic Mahram Relations
List the three categories: two nurslings of one breast become mahram; wet nurse is mahram to the nursling and to the nursling's children; wet nurse is mahram to the child of the nursling's child.
The wet nurse is called 'murḍiʿa' (with fatha) and the nursing woman is 'murḍiʿa' (with kasra).
2
Understand the Rule for Mixed Milk
According to Abu Hanifa, milk mixed with solid food does not prohibit at all, because the solid subsumes the liquid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it prohibits if the milk is predominant. For liquid mixtures (water, medicine), predominance is considered.
Cooking the mixture removes prohibition entirely by consensus.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Ghalab
Abu Yusuf defines ghalab as changing the color and taste of the mixture; if only one changes, milk is predominant. Muhammad defines it as the mixture no longer being considered milk. For two women's milk, Abu Yusuf considers the greater quantity; Muhammad and Zufar consider both equally.
The text prefers Muhammad's view as more apparent and precautionary (aẓhar wa aḥwaṭ).
4
Examine the Rationale (Illa) from Hadith
The hadith 'al-rada' ma anbata al-lahm wa nashara al-azm' proves that prohibition requires nourishment leading to growth. A mixture that does not achieve this (e.g., milk diluted beyond effectiveness) does not establish prohibition.
This refutes the Shafi'i position that five complete feedings from a diluted mixture suffice.
5
Apply to Modern Cases
Consider scenarios like infant formula mixed with water or food. If the milk component is not predominant and cannot independently support growth, no fosterage ties are created.
This prevents unintended mahram relations in everyday situations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا حل بين رضيعي ثدي وبين مرضعة وولد مرضعتها، وولد ولدها، واللبن المخلوط بالطعام لا يحرم، ويعتبر الغالب لو بماءٍ ودواء، ولبن شاة وامرأة أخرى أي لو كان الاختلاط بين رضيعي ثدي: الأنهما أخوان وأراد بهما الصبي والصبية اجتمعا على ثدي واحد في مدة الرضاع لم يجز لأحدهما أن يتزوج بالأخرى، فغلب المذكر على المؤنث كما في القمرين والأبوين والمراد اجتماعهما من حيث المكان بأن رضع أحدهما ثدي امرأة رضعه الآخر، بين المرضعة بالفتح وبين ولد ولد المرضعة بالكسر؛ لأنه ولد أخيها من الرضاعة. لا يحرم: [سواء كان الطعام غالباً أو مساوياً.] عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن غير المائع يستتبع المائع، وعندهما: يحرم إذا كان اللبن غالباً، وهذا الخلاف في غير المطبوخ، وأما إذا طبخ فلا يحرم اتفاقاً مطلقاً، وشرط القدوري على قول أبي حنيفة أن يكون الطعام مستبينا كالثريد قيل: هذا إذا لم يتقاطر اللبن عند حمل اللقمة، وإن تقاطر تثبت به الحرمة وقيل لا تثبت بكل حال وهو الصحيح. ويعتبر الغالب إلخ لأن فيه إنبات اللحم وإنشاء العظم، وهو المعتبر في الباب؛ لقوله عليه: "الرضاع ما أنبت اللحم وأنشر العظم"، وقال الشافعي: إذا جعل في جب من الماء قدر ما يحصل به خمس رضعات من اللبن تثبت به الحرمة، سواء كان غالباً أو مغلوباً؛ لأنه شرب لبن المرأة، وبه قال أحمد، وعند مالك: يعتبر المشوب ما لم يستهلك أثر اللبن فيما خلط به، ونحن نقول: إن اللبن بالخلط صار مستهلكاً فلا يحصل به التغذي، ولا إنبات اللحم، ولا إنشاء العظم، بخلاف الغالب كما لو حلف لا يشرب لبناً لا يحنث بشرب الماء الذي فيه أجزاء اللبن واختلف في تفسير الغالب، فعند أبي يوسف هو أن يغير المخلوط لون اللبن وطعمه، أما لو غير أحدهما فاللبن غالب، وعند محمد: هو أن يخرج الخلط اللبن من أن يكون لبنا. ولبن شاة: لأن المغلوب لا يظهر فصار كالمستهلك. وامرأة أخرى [أي وكذلك يعتبر الغالب لو اختلط بلبن امرأة أخرى عندهما خلافاً لمحمد] أي إذا اختلط لبن امرأتين يتعلق التحريم بأغلبهما عند أبي يوسف، وإذا تساوى لبنهما يثبت التحريم من المرأتين إجماعاً، وقال محمد وزفر يتعلق بهما التحريم كيف ما كان، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه يغلب الجنس بل يكثره الجنس فلا يصير مستهلكاً؛ لاتحاد المقصود، ولهما: أن الأقل تابع للأكثر فصار كاللبن والماء، وقول محمد أظهر وأحوط
And no marriage is permissible between two nurslings of one breast and between the wet nurse and the child of her nursing, and the child of her nursing's child, and milk mixed with food does not prohibit, and the predominant is considered if with water and medicine, and milk of a goat and another woman. That is, if the mixing between two nurslings of one breast: they are two brothers, and he meant by them a boy and a girl who both suckled from one breast during the period of nursing; it is not permissible for one of them to marry the other, so the masculine is given precedence over the feminine as in 'al-qamarayn' (the two moons) and 'al-abawayn' (the two parents). And what is meant is their coming together in terms of place, by one of them sucking the breast of a woman that the other also sucked, not in terms of time, meaning they both suckle at the same time, nor that they both suckle the right breast or the left breast together. Rather, what is meant is that they both suckle from this woman in whatever manner. And between the wet nurse and the child of her nursing: i.e., the nursing of the wet nurse. And meeting at her breast is not required here so that the issue is not repeated. Its description: a woman nurses a foreign female, so this foreign female becomes prohibited to the child of the wet nurse, whether she nursed her own child or not, because her child is the brother of the foreign female in all cases. And the child of her child: i.e., also no marriage is permissible between the wet nurse and the child of the child of the wet nurse, because he is the son of her brother through nursing. (The milk mixed with food) does not prohibit: whether the food is predominant or equal, according to Abu Hanifa, because non-liquid subsumes liquid. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): it prohibits if the milk is predominant. This difference is for uncooked (food). As for when it is cooked, it does not prohibit absolutely by consensus. Al-Quduri stipulated according to Abu Hanifa that the food must be distinct, like tharid. It is said this is when the milk does not drip when carrying the morsel; if it drips, prohibition is established. And it is said it is not established in any case, and that is the correct view. And the predominant is considered etc., because it contains growth of flesh and creation of bone, and that is what is considered in this chapter due to his saying peace be upon him: 'Nursing is what grows flesh and strengthens bone.' Al-Shafi'i said: if placed in a container of water an amount that achieves five sucklings of milk, prohibition is established whether it is predominant or overpowered, because the child drank the woman's milk. Ahmad said the same. According to Malik: the mixture is considered as long as the trace of milk has not been consumed in what it is mixed with. And we say: by mixing, the milk becomes consumed, so nourishment, growth of flesh, and creation of bone are not achieved, contrary to when it is predominant, just as if one swears not to drink milk, he does not break his oath by drinking water containing parts of milk. And they differed in interpreting 'predominant'. According to Abu Yusuf: it is that the mixture changes the color and taste of the milk. If it changes only one, then the milk is predominant. According to Muhammad: it is that the mixture takes the milk out of being milk. And the milk of a goat: because the overpowered does not appear, so it becomes like consumed. And another woman: i.e., similarly, the predominant is considered if mixed with the milk of another woman according to them (the two), contrary to Muhammad. That is, if the milk of two women mixes, prohibition attaches to the more predominant according to Abu Yusuf. If their milk is equal, prohibition is established from both women by consensus. Muhammad and Zufar said: prohibition attaches to both no matter what, and that is a narration from Abu Hanifa, because gender is strengthened by the genus and is not consumed due to unity of purpose. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the lesser follows the greater, so it becomes like milk and water. And Muhammad's view is more apparent and more precautionary.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq deals with the fundamental rules of fosterage (rada'). It begins by defining who becomes mahram through nursing: two children who nurse from the same woman become foster siblings and cannot marry each other. The wet nurse herself becomes mahram to the child she nurses and to that child's descendants. The passage then addresses a key issue: when milk is mixed with other substances like food, water, or medicine. The ruling is that mere mixing does not automatically create prohibition; what matters is whether the milk is predominant (ghalib) such that it can nourish and promote growth. Abu Hanifa holds that mixing with solid food (non-liquid) nullifies the milk's effect entirely because the solid subsumes the liquid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree, saying if the milk is predominant in the mixture, prohibition is established. There is also a discussion of mixing milk with another woman's milk: Abu Yusuf looks at which milk is greater in quantity; Muhammad and Zufar say both are considered regardless. The passage also notes the definitions of 'predominant' and includes the famous hadith that nursing is what grows flesh and strengthens bone, which is the underlying rationale (illa) for prohibition. The commentary then refutes the Shafi'i position that even diluted milk can prohibit if five full feedings are achieved, emphasizing that the milk must be effective for growth.

Key Terms
رضيعي ثدي (raḍīʿay thady): Two children who nursed from the same breast of a woman.
اللبن المخلوط (al-laban al-makhlūṭ): Breastmilk mixed with another substance such as food, water, medicine, or another woman's milk.
الغالب (al-ghālib): The milk being predominant in the mixture such that it changes the mixture's color and taste (Abu Yusuf) or takes the mixture out of being milk (Muhammad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if breastmilk is mixed with solid food (like tharid) and the food is distinct (mastabin), what is the ruling?
A) Prohibition is established because milk is present.
B) Prohibition is not established because the solid food subsumes the liquid milk.
C) Prohibition is established only if the milk is predominant.
D) Prohibition is established if five full feedings were possible.

Key Takeaway
Fosterage prohibition hinges on effective nourishment; mere presence of milk in a mixture does not suffice unless it is predominant and promotes growth.

Effect of Incomplete Ghusl on Raj'ah Period
Ruling on how forgetting a body part during ghusl affects the revocation period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raj'ah when a part of the body is left unwashed during ghusl and explain how the size of the missed part (limb vs. less than limb) determines the outcome via istihsan.

Core Idea
Istihsan prioritizes practical ease: a small unwashed part dries quickly, so raj'ah ends; a limb does not.

This passage from the chapter of Raj'ah addresses a nuanced scenario: a woman in her 'iddah performs ghusl after menstruation but forgets to wash a part of her body. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes based on the size of the missed area, employing istihsan to override strict qiyas. The size of the unwashed part determines whether her husband's right to take her back (raj'ah) ends or continues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
The act is the performance of ghusl by a woman in her revocable 'iddah (after a first or second divorce) following menstruation. The ruling concerns whether her ghusl is considered effective enough to terminate her husband's right of raj'ah.
The ghusl is for purification from menstruation, not from janabah.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios: less than a limb vs. limb or more
If the missed part is less than a full limb, the raj'ah period ends (the husband cannot take her back). If it is a limb or more, raj'ah remains (the husband can still take her back). A 'limb' here means a body part that is customarily considered a limb, like an arm, leg, or head.
The distinction hinges on the size and drying time of the unwashed area.
3
Analyze the istihsan rationale
The default qiyas would suggest that any missing part invalidates the complete removal of impurity, so raj'ah should remain. But istihsan prefers a practical outcome: small areas dry quickly after being touched by water, so they are considered effectively washed. Large areas do not dry quickly, so the ghusl is deemed incomplete for the purpose of ending raj'ah.
Istihsan here overrides analogy (qiyas) due to practical ease and custom.
4
Note the precautionary requirements (ihtiyat)
Even when raj'ah ends (less than limb), the woman is not permitted to marry another man or be approached sexually until she washes that specific spot or a full prayer time passes. This is a precaution for protection of lineage (furuj).
The ruling on raj'ah is separate from the ruling on permissibility of marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتصلي، ولو اغتسال ولو اغتسلت ونسيت أقل من عضو تنقطع، ولو عضواً لا. أي إن اغتسلت ونسيت شيئاً من بدنها لم يصبه الماء إن كان أقل من عضو انقطعت الرجعة؛ لأن تسارع الجفاف إليه بعد أصابته بالماء غير بعيد لاسيما في الحر الشديد لكن لا يحل لها التزوج، وكذا لا يحل قربانها حتى تغسله احتياطاً في أمر الفروج، أو يمضي عليها وقت صلاة، وإن كان عضواً فما فوقها لا تنقطع؛ لأنه كثير لا يتسارع إليه الجفاف وهذا استحساناً، والقياس في العضو الكامل أن تنقطع الرجعة؛ لأنها غسلت الأكثر ، وله حكم الكل، وفيه قياس آخر أن الرجعة تبقى في ما دون العضو أيضاً؛ لأن حكم الحدث لا يتجزأ زوالاً كما لا يتجزأ ،ثبوتاً، فبقيت على ما كانت قبل الاغتسال، وجه الاستحسان، وهو الفرق بين العضو وما دونه أن ما دون العضو يتسارع إليه الجفاف لقلته.
And she prays, and if she performs ghusl and forgets less than a limb, raj'ah ends; if a limb, it does not. That is, if she performs ghusl and forgets something of her body that water did not reach, if it was less than a limb, the raj'ah is cut off because the rapid drying of that part after being hit by water is not far-fetched, especially in extreme heat, but it is not lawful for her to marry, nor is it lawful to approach her until she washes it out of caution in matters of private parts, or a prayer time passes over her. And if it was a limb or more, it is not cut off because it is much and does not dry quickly. This is istihsan. The qiyas in the case of a complete limb is that raj'ah is cut off because she washed most, and it has the ruling of the whole. There is another qiyas that raj'ah remains even in less than a limb because the ruling of impurity does not divide in removal just as it does not divide in establishment, so it remains as it was before ghusl. The face of istihsan is the distinction between a limb and less than it: that less than a limb dries quickly due to its smallness.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter of Raj'ah regarding the effect of an incomplete ghusl (ritual bath) on the revocation period. The matn states: if a woman in her 'iddah performs ghusl (after menstruation) and forgets to wash a part of her body, if that part is less than a full limb, the raj'ah period ends; if it is a limb or more, it does not end. The commentary explains the reasoning: for less than a limb, even though the water did not reach it, the area is small and would dry quickly after being touched by water, so it is assumed she completed the ghusl in terms of the legal effect. However, she is not permitted to marry or be approached sexually until she washes that spot or a prayer time passes (as a precaution). For a limb or more, the area is large and does not dry quickly, so the ghusl is considered incomplete and raj'ah remains. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas (analogy) would suggest that washing most of the body should suffice for the whole, thus ending raj'ah even for a limb, or conversely, that impurity cannot be partially removed, so raj'ah should remain for even a small part. Istihsan gives precedence to the practical reality of rapid drying for small areas. The text mentions that Imam Zufar agreed with the istihsan, while Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held that tayammum is a necessary purification and does not affect this analogy.

Key Terms
الرجعة (ar-raj'ah): The right of a husband to take back his wife during her 'iddah without a new marriage contract.
الغسل (al-ghusl): Full ritual washing of the body, required after menstruation or sexual impurity.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside strict analogy for a more practical or equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman in her 'iddah performs ghusl after haydh but forgets to wash her entire right foot (considered a limb). Does the raj'ah period end according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Yes, because she washed most of her body.
B) No, because a limb or more left unwashed means raj'ah continues.
C) Yes, because the foot is small and dries quickly.
D) No, because only the head is considered a limb.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between forgetting less than a limb (raj'ah ends) and a limb or more (raj'ah continues), based on istihsan considering rapid drying of small areas.

Definition and General Rulings of 'Iddah
Defines 'iddah and its components linguistically and legally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition, cause, condition, and pillar of 'iddah according to the Hanafi school and explain why it is a right of Allah.

Core Idea
'Iddah is a waiting period that is a right of Allah, triggered by a confirmed marriage, and cannot be waived by consent.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational concepts of 'iddah (waiting period) as defined in the Hanafi tradition. You will learn not only the linguistic and legal definitions but also the essential components that make 'iddah obligatory and its unique nature as a right of the Shari'ah. Understanding these basics is crucial for mastering the subsequent rulings on divorce and its aftermath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and legal definition
First, understand that linguistically 'iddah means counting or waiting, and legally it is a known waiting period after the removal of marriage or its semblance, consummated or not, or after death.
The linguistic root emphasizes measurement and anticipation.
2
Determine the cause (sabab) of obligation
According to the Hanafi school, the cause is a marriage confirmed by delivery (taslim) or its equivalent, such as valid seclusion (khilwah sahihah).
This distinguishes Hanafi from schools that require only a valid contract.
3
Identify the condition (shart)
The condition for 'iddah to be obligatory is the occurrence of separation (furqah) between the spouses.
Without separation, 'iddah does not commence.
4
Identify the pillar (rukn)
The pillar of 'iddah is the set of prohibitions that become fixed due to it, such as the prohibition of marrying the woman's sister or a fifth wife.
These prohibitions define the essence of 'iddah.
5
Understand the general rulings
Recognize that 'iddah is a right of Allah (haqq al-shar'), so it cannot be dropped by the woman, and she may not go out even with the husband's permission. Also, two 'iddahs can overlap, but the right of a slave does not.
The overlapping rule prevents unnecessary extension of waiting periods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العدة: هي لغةً مصدر من "عد يعد" يقال: عددت بشيء أي أحصيته. بالكسر الإحصاء، وبالضم الامتداد للأمر، وشرعاً : انتظار مدة معلومة تلزم المرأة بعد زوال النكاح، أو شبهته المتأكد بالدخول حقيقة أو حكماً، أو الموت، وسبب وجوبه عندنا: النكاح المتأكد بالتسليم أو ما يجري مجراه، وشرطها: الفرقة، وركنها: حرمات ثابتة بها كنكاح أختها وأربع سواها، وهي حق الشرع؛ ولهذا لا تسقط لو أسقطها، فلا يحل لها الخروج لو أذن له الزوج، وتتداخل العدتان، ولا يتداخل حق العبد، وأورد العدة بعد وجوه الفرقة من الطلاق والإيلاء والخلع واللعان وأحكام العنين؛ لأن العدة أثر الطلاق، والأثر يتبع المؤثر.
Chapter of 'Iddah: It is linguistically a source from 'ada ya'uddu: one says 'adadtu bi shay' i.e. I counted it. With kasra it means counting, with damm it means waiting for a matter. Legally: waiting a known period that becomes incumbent upon a woman after the removal of marriage, or its resemblance confirmed by actual or legal consummation, or death. Its cause according to us: marriage confirmed by delivery or what takes its place. Its condition: separation. Its pillar: prohibitions established by it, like marrying her sister or four others besides her. It is a right of the Shari'ah; therefore it is not dropped if she drops it, and she may not go out even if the husband permits. Two 'iddahs overlap, but the right of the slave does not overlap. He mentioned 'iddah after the types of separation: divorce, ila, khul', li'an, and rulings of the impotent, because 'iddah is the effect of divorce, and the effect follows the effective cause.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage is a definition and general rulings section from a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins by defining 'iddah linguistically and legally. Linguistically, 'iddah with kasra means counting, and with damm means waiting. Legally, it is a waiting period incumbent on a woman after the end of a marriage or its semblance that was confirmed by consummation (actual or constructive) or death. The cause (sabab) of its obligation according to the Hanafi school is a marriage that is confirmed by delivery (taslim) or its equivalent, such as khilwah sahihah. The condition (shart) is separation between the spouses. The pillar (rukn) consists of prohibitions that become fixed due to the 'iddah, such as the prohibition of marrying the woman's sister or a fifth wife. 'Iddah is a right of Allah (haqq al-shar'), hence it cannot be dropped by the woman's waiver, and she is not permitted to leave the house even with the husband's permission. The commentary notes that two 'iddahs overlap (tadakhul), e.g., if a woman is divorced during her 'iddah from a previous marriage, they run concurrently, but the right of the slave (in matters like manumission) does not overlap. The author placed the chapter on 'iddah after the types of separation because 'iddah is an effect, and the effect follows its cause.

Key Terms
العدة (al-'iddah): A waiting period incumbent on a woman after removal of marriage or its semblance, consummated or not, or after husband's death.
سبب الوجوب (sabab al-wujub): The cause that makes 'iddah obligatory: a marriage confirmed by delivery or its equivalent.
ركن العدة (rukn al-'iddah): The prohibitions that become fixed due to 'iddah, like marrying a close relative of the woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the cause (sabab) of 'iddah?
A) Simply the act of divorce
B) Marriage confirmed by delivery or its equivalent
C) The husband's death
D) The woman's request

Key Takeaway
'Iddah is a fixed waiting period that is a right of Allah, triggered by a confirmed marriage, and its pillar is the prohibitions that arise from it.

Woman's Statement on Iddah with Oath
Ruling on woman's iddah claim with oath and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on acceptance of a woman's claim regarding completion of her iddah, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the requirement of an oath, and apply the analogy to the depositary (mowda') to justify the ruling.

Core Idea
A woman's claim of iddah completion is accepted with an oath because she is trustworthy, but the oath is required due to suspicion.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a woman claims her iddah has ended, her word is generally accepted, but with a condition. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies that she must take an oath — a ruling that is not without internal dispute. We will examine the proof by analogy to a depositary and the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Ruling
What is the default ruling for the woman's statement regarding iddah completion? The text states: 'her statement is accepted with the oath.'
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Trace the Proof by Analogy
How does the author justify the oath? The woman is compared to a depositary (mowda') who is trusted but may be lying, so an oath is required.
Qiyas: both are amina (trustworthy) but tuhmah al-kidhb (suspicion of lying) exists.
3
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
What is the dispute? Abu Hanifa holds that no oath is required; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) require the oath.
The text sides with Sahibayn.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Which position is relied upon for fatwa? The mufta bihi is that the woman must swear, according to Fath and Mustakhlas.
This is the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالقول لها مع الحلف أي للمرأة رجل فالقول لها مع الحلف لأنها أمينة كالمودَع إذا ادعى رد الوديعة أو هلاكها (ع)] أي إذا قالت المعتدة: "مضت عدتي" والمدة تحتمل ذلك، فلو بالشهور فالقدر المذكور، ولو بالحيض فأقلها للحرة ستون يوماً، والأمة أربعون، فالقول للمرأة مع اليمين؛ لأنها أمينة والتحليف قولهما؛ لأنها اتهمت بالكذب، فتحلف كالمودع، ولا تحلف على قول الإمام. (فتح)، مستخلص)
So the statement (of the woman) is accepted with the oath. Meaning for the woman... the statement is accepted with the oath because she is trustworthy, like the depositary when he claims return or loss of the deposit. (From 'Ayni): i.e. when the woman in iddah says 'my iddah has passed' and the period could accommodate that, if by months then the mentioned amount, if by menses then the minimum for a free woman is sixty days and for a slave forty days, so the statement of the woman is accepted with the oath because she is trustworthy, and the swearing is necessary because she is accused of lying, so she swears like the depositary. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, she does not swear. (From Fath, Mustakhlas).
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof. The text opens by stating the ruling: the woman's word regarding completion of her iddah is accepted, but she must take an oath. The commentator clarifies that this applies when the duration is plausible (e.g., 60 days for a free woman based on minimum iddah for a husband who travels). The proof is analogy (qiyas) to a depositary (mowda') who claims return or loss of a deposit: both are trusted (amina), but due to suspicion of lying, an oath is required. The commentator notes a difference: Abu Hanifa holds that she does not swear, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require the oath. The relied-upon position is to require the oath, as stated in Fath.

Key Terms
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarriage.
يمين (yameen): An oath sworn by Allah, used to affirm a claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the woman's statement about her iddah accepted with an oath according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the iddah is a light matter.
B) Because she is trusted like a depositary over her own body.
C) Because the Quran explicitly says so.
D) Because the husband cannot dispute it.

Key Takeaway
A woman's claim of iddah completion is accepted with an oath due to suspicion of lying, following the Sahibayn view.

Obligation of Wife's Maintenance and its Amount
Establishes the ruling, evidence, and amount of spousal maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wife's maintenance, identify its proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, explain the method for determining the amount based on both spouses' conditions, and apply the ruling in cases where the wife withholds herself for dower.

Core Idea
Wife's maintenance is wajib; its amount considers both spouses' financial status, balancing the husband's capacity and the wife's need.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq establishes the fundamental ruling of spousal maintenance (nafaqah) in the Hanafi school. It not only declares the obligation but also provides the textual proofs and clarifies the critical question of how much maintenance is owed. You will see how the Hanafi school derives a balanced position that considers both the husband's ability and the wife's needs, and how this differs from other schools and even within the early Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Locate the core claim: 'Maintenance is obligatory for the wife upon her husband.' Note that this applies absolutely, regardless of whether the marriage is consummated, her religion, or her financial status.
The Arabic phrase 'لِلزَّوْجَةِ' indicates the wife is the recipient; the husband is the obligor.
2
Trace the proofs (dalil)
Find the four proofs cited: two Quranic verses (65:7, 2:233), the Sunnah (Hadith of the Farewell Sermon and the instruction to Hind), ijma, and rational argument (as compensation for confinement).
The rational argument is unique: nafaqah is a return for the wife's being confined to the marriage.
3
Examine the amount determination
The text states maintenance is 'according to the condition of both' spouses. If both are affluent, affluent maintenance; if both poor, poor maintenance; if she is poor and he is rich, it is between the two levels.
This is the author's choice and the fatwa; al-Karkhi and al-Shafi'i said only the husband's condition matters.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to the opposing view
The Hanafi response uses the Hadith of Hind to show the wife's need is considered. The husband's capacity is for the immediate payment; any shortfall becomes a debt.
Combining both proofs (Quran and Hadith) is the usul method.
5
Apply the rule when the wife withholds herself
The phrase 'even if she is preventing herself' means if she holds back to collect her dower, maintenance is still obligatory because she is preventing by right, not as a nashizah.
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifah says no drop; the two disciples say it drops after consummation unless she is below puberty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
باب النفقة
أي في بيان أحكامها
تجب النفقة للزوجة على زوجها والكسوة بقدر حالهما ولو مانعة نفسها . الزوجين
من
باب النفقة: [وهي في اللغة ما ينفقه الإنسان على عياله. (فتح)] أورد مباحث النفقة في ذيل كتاب الطلاق؛ لأن من جملتها نفقة المطلقة، وبعضهم أوردها في ذيل كتاب النكاح لترتب نفقة المنكوحة، وبعضهم في كتاب على حدة لما فيها من نفقة ذوي الأرحام والمماليك وهي في اللغة: ما ينفقه الإنسان على عياله، وفي الشرع: الطعام والكسوة والسكنى. قيل: هي مشتقة النفوق بمعنى الهلاك أو النفاق بمعنى الرواج؛ لأن بها هلاك المال أو لأنها تروج في مصالح الحال، ونفقة الغير على الغير تجب بثلاثة أشياء: بالزوجية وبالقرابة وبالملك، وكذا تحب بسبب حبس النفس لمصالح الغير كالمضارب والوصي، أو لمصالح العامة كالمفتي والقاضي والوالي والعامل في الصدقات والمقاتلة. (فتح)
للزوجة: [مطلقاً سواء كانت تزف إلى مبيت زوجها أو لم تزف، وسواء كانت مسلمة أو كافرة، غنية أو فقيرة مدخولاً بها أو لا. (مسكين)] بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع وضرب من المعقول، أما الكتاب: فقوله تعالى : اليُنْفِقْ ذُو سَعَةٍ مِنْ سَعَتِه الله (الطلاق:۷)، وقوله تعالى: وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ رِزْقُهُنَّ وَكِسْوَتُهُنَّ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ ﴾ (البقرة:٢٣٣)، وأما السنة: روي أنه عليها قال في خطبة الوداع: "اتقوا الله في "النساء" إلى أن قال: "ولهن عليكم رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف"، وأما الإجماع: فإن الأمة أجمعت على أن النفقة والسكنى واجبتان للزوجة على زوجها، وأما المعقول: فلأن النفقة تجب جزاء الاحتباس، وهذا إذا كان النكاح صحيحا [تبيين الحقائق: ٣٠١/٣] على زوجها غنيا أو فقيرا حاضرا أو غائباً . (ط) والكسوة أي تجب الكسوة لها عليه أيضاً. (ع) بقدر حالهما: [ أي حال الزوجين في اليسار والإعسار. (ط، ع] أي تجب النفقة والكسوة لها عليه بقدر حالهما في اليسار والإعسار ، فإن كان الزوجان موسرين كان لها نفقة اليسار، وإن كانا معسرين كان لها نفقة الإعسار وإن كانت معسرة والزوج موسر فنفقتها ما دون نفقة الموسرات فوق نفقة المعسرات، وهذا اختيار المصنف، وعليه الفتوى، وقال الكرخي والشافعي: يعتبر حال الزوج؛ لقوله تعالى: وَلِيُنْفِقْ ذُو سَعَةٍ مِنْ سَعَتِهِ ولنا: قوله عليها لهند امرأة أبي سفيان: خذي من مال زوجك ما يكفيك وولدك بالمعروف" اعتبر حالها. والفقيرة لا تفتقر إلى كفاية الموسرات، فلا معنى للزيادة، وأما النص فنحن نقول بموجبه : أنه مخاطب بقدر وسعه، والباقي دين في ذمته ومعنى قوله: "بالمعروف الوسط، وهو الواجب، واعتبر حالهما معاً جمعاً بين الآية والحديث؛ لأن الآية تقتضي اعتبار حاله والحديث يقتضي اعتبار حالها فاعتبرنا حالهما عملاً بهما. (فتح، مص) ولو مانعة إلخ: [واصل بما قبلها أي ولو كانت المرأة مانعة من التسليم تجب النفقة. (ع)] متصل بما قبله أي تحب النفقة لها وإن امتنعت من تسليم نفسها لأجل قبض المهر الذي تعورف تقديمه في البلاد والزمان؛ لأنه منع بحق للمهر، لا ناشزة وصغيرةً لا توطأ ومحبوسة بدين ومغصوبة وحاجةً مع غير الزوج، لتقصير من جهته، فلا تسقط النفقة به وإن كان بعد الدخول عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: تسقط إلا إذا كانت دون البلوغ؛ لعدم صحة تسليم الأب، وقوله: "ولا" ناشزة
Book of Divorce. Chapter of Maintenance. That is, explaining its rulings. Maintenance is obligatory for the wife upon her husband, and clothing according to the condition of both, even if she prevents herself (from delivery). The two spouses. From the Chapter of Maintenance: [It is linguistically what a person spends on his dependents. (Fath)] The topics of maintenance are presented at the end of the Book of Divorce because among them is the maintenance of the divorced woman; some presented them at the end of the Book of Nikah due to the connection to the maintenance of the married woman; and some in a separate book due to the maintenance of relatives and slaves. Linguistically: it is what a person spends on his dependents. In Sacred Law: food, clothing, and housing. It is said: it is derived from 'nufuq' meaning destruction or 'nifaq' meaning circulation; because through it wealth perishes or because it circulates in the interests of the state. Maintenance of one person for another is obligatory due to three things: marriage, kinship, and ownership. Similarly, it is obligatory due to detaining oneself for the interests of others, like the mudarib and executor, or for public interests like the mufti, judge, governor, zakat collector, and fighters. (Fath) For the wife: [Absolutely, whether she is brought to the husband's bed or not, whether Muslim or disbeliever, rich or poor, consummated or not. (Miskin)] By the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and a type of rational proof. As for the Book: His saying, exalted: 'Let the one of ample means spend from his ample means' (At-Talaq 65:7), and His saying: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable' (Al-Baqarah 2:233). As for the Sunnah: It is narrated that he (peace be upon him) said in the Farewell Sermon: 'Fear Allah regarding women... and said: 'Their provision and clothing are due from you according to what is acceptable.'' As for consensus: The ummah has agreed that maintenance and lodging are obligatory for the wife upon her husband. As for the rational: because maintenance is obligatory as recompense for detaining (her). This applies if the marriage is valid. [Tabyin al-Haqaiq: 3/301] upon her husband, whether he is rich or poor, present or absent. (T) And clothing: i.e., clothing is also obligatory for her upon him. (A) According to the condition of both: [i.e., the condition of the two spouses in wealth and poverty. (T, A)] i.e., maintenance and clothing are obligatory for her upon him according to their condition in wealth and poverty. If both spouses are affluent, she gets affluent maintenance; if both are poor, she gets poor maintenance; if she is poor and the husband is affluent, her maintenance is less than that of affluent women and above that of poor women. This is the author's choice, and the fatwa is upon it. Al-Karkhi and al-Shafi'i said: The husband's condition is considered due to His saying: 'Let the one of ample means spend from his ample means.' Our evidence: His saying (peace be upon him) to Hind, the wife of Abu Sufyan: 'Take from your husband's wealth what suffices you and your child with good measure.' He considered her condition. The poor woman does not need the sufficiency of affluent women, so there is no meaning for increase. As for the text, we accept it: he is addressed according to his capacity, and the remainder is a debt upon his liability. The meaning of 'with good measure' is the middle, which is obligatory. We consider the condition of both together, combining the verse and hadith; because the verse requires considering his condition, and the hadith requires considering her condition, so we consider both conditions to act upon both. (Fath, Mus) 'Even if she is preventing' etc.: [Connected to what preceded, i.e., even if the woman is preventing delivery, maintenance is obligatory. (A)] It is connected to what preceded, i.e., maintenance is obligatory for her even if she refrains from surrendering herself for the purpose of receiving the dower that is customarily advanced in lands and times; because it is a rightful prevention for the dower, not rebelliousness, nor a minor girl who is not slept with, nor a woman imprisoned for debt, nor a kidnapped woman, nor a woman performing hajj with someone other than her husband. (This is) because the failure is from his side, so maintenance is not dropped by it, even if it was after consummation according to Abu Hanifah. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it drops unless she is below puberty, because the father's delivery is not valid. And his saying: 'and not rebellious.'
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, defining the obligation of spousal maintenance (nafaqah) in the Hanafi school. It begins with the definition of nafaqah linguistically and legally, and the causes for its obligation: marriage, kinship, and ownership. The focus then narrows to the wife: maintenance is obligatory for her absolutely, regardless of whether the marriage is consummated, her religion, wealth, or presence. The proofs are drawn from the Qur'an (two verses), the Sunnah (the Prophet's instruction to Hind), consensus (ijma'), and rational argument (as compensation for the wife being confined to the marriage). The amount is determined by the financial status of both spouses jointly, not just the husband's, based on combining the Qur'anic command (considering his capacity) and the hadith (considering her needs). The author's preferred view, which is the basis for fatwa, is that the wife's condition is also considered, especially when the husband is wealthy and she is poor. Finally, the passage clarifies that if the wife withholds herself to collect her dower (mahr), maintenance is still obligatory because she is preventing herself rightfully. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifah holds that maintenance is not dropped whether before or after consummation, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it drops after consummation unless the wife is below the age of puberty.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance: linguistically what a person spends on dependents; legally, food, clothing, and housing obligatory upon the husband for the wife.
الزوجية (al-zawjiyyah): The marital bond, which is one of the three causes for obligation of nafaqah.
المهر (al-mahr): The dower or bridal gift, which the wife may rightfully withhold herself until she receives it customarily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the amount of maintenance (nafaqah) for a wife when the husband is wealthy but the wife is poor?
A) Maintenance of affluent women.
B) Maintenance of poor women.
C) Between the two, avoiding excess.
D) It is not obligatory at all.

Key Takeaway
Wife's maintenance is wajib on the husband, with the amount determined by both spouses' financial conditions, and it is not forfeited by rightful prevention for dower.

Nushuz and Its Effect on Maintenance
Defines nashiz and states when maintenance drops

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define nushuz according to the Hanafi school and state the condition under which maintenance drops and revives.

Core Idea
Maintenance is compensation for confinement; when confinement breaks due to nushuz, maintenance stops.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi definition of nushuz (disobedience) and its direct consequence on the wife's entitlement to maintenance (nafaqah). Understanding this link is essential because it shows that maintenance is not an unconditional right but a compensation tied to a specific behavior: the wife's confinement (ihtibas) in her husband's home. The text also highlights exceptional cases where the wife is not considered nashiz even if she leaves, and explains that nushuz ends upon return.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term and its ruling context
Locate the term nushuz in the passage and note that it is defined in the context of maintenance (nafaqah). The ruling is that maintenance is not wajib for a nashiz wife.
2
Isolate the legal basis: confinement (ihtibas)
The passage states that maintenance is compensation (jaza) for ihtibas. Understand that ihtibas means the wife's remaining in the home and being available for marital relations. Without ihtibas, there is no entitlement.
This is a key principle: the wife's obedience and confinement are the consideration for maintenance.
3
Recognize the exceptions where maintenance drops even without physical departure
The text lists three scenarios where the prompt dower is paid, all dower is deferred, or the wife waives her dower. In these cases, the wife has the right to leave, so her remaining is not obligatory; if she leaves, she is nashiz.
These exceptions hinge on the dower situation, not on the act of leaving alone.
4
Understand the revival of maintenance upon return
The passage says: 'If the nashiz wife returns to her husband's house, she has maintenance.' This means nushuz is a temporary state that ends when the wife ends her disobedience.
Maintenance is not permanently forfeited; it resumes when confinement is restored.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: "ولا" ناشزة" النشوز في اصطلاح الفقهاء "خروج المرأة من منزل الزوج، ومنعها نفسها منه بغير حق" بأن أوفى مهرها أو كان كله مؤجلاً أو وهبت منه حيث تسقط النفقة به لعدم الاحتباس؛ لأنها جزاء الاحتباس ولو عادت الناشزة إلى بيت زوجها فلها النفقة. (مستخلص، عيني) للمهر: أي لأجل قبض المهر المعجل والذي كله مؤجل. (ط، ع) ناشزة: أي لا تجب النفقة والكسوة لو كانت ناشزة أي خارجة من بيته بغير حق حتى تعود. (ط)
His saying: "and not nashiz." Nashiz in the terminology of jurists is "the wife leaving her husband's home and preventing herself from him without right," such as when her prompt dower is paid or all of it is deferred or she has waived it, where maintenance falls away due to lack of confinement because maintenance is compensation for confinement. If the nashiz wife returns to her husband's house, she has maintenance. (Mukhtasar, Ayni) "For the dower" means for taking the prompt dower or that which is all deferred. (T, A) "Nashiz" means maintenance and clothing are not obligatory if she is nashiz, i.e., leaving his house without right until she returns. (T)
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage defines the legal concept of nashiz (disobedience) as it relates to the wife's entitlement to maintenance (nafaqah). According to the Hanafi school, maintenance is compensation for the wife's confinement (ihtibas) in her husband's home and her readiness for sexual relations. If she leaves the home without a valid right or withholds herself from him, she loses this entitlement because the basis of maintenance—confinement—is absent. The text specifies that maintenance falls in three scenarios: when the prompt dower is fully paid, when all dower is deferred, or when she has waived her dower. In these cases, her remaining in the home is no longer obligatory for her, and thus she is considered disobedient. However, if she returns to the marital home and ends her disobedience, her right to maintenance revives. The passage also clarifies that 'for the dower' refers to the receipt of the prompt dower or the entirely deferred dower, and that nashiz specifically means leaving the husband's house without right until she returns.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushūz): The wife's leaving the marital home or preventing access to herself without a valid right.
احتباس (iḥtibās): The wife's confinement in the husband's home and being available for marital relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the wife's entitlement to maintenance in Hanafi fiqh?
A) The husband's ability to pay
B) The wife's confinement (ihtibas)
C) The payment of dower
D) The marital contract itself

Key Takeaway
Maintenance is compensation for confinement; nushuz breaks confinement and thus breaks maintenance.
